The Fourth Objection: Gabriel as Teacher
Objection and refutation regarding Gabriel's teaching role

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the objection that Gabriel is superior because he taught the Prophet is refuted by distinguishing conveyance from true teaching.

Core Idea
Angels convey; only Allah teaches.

This lesson tackles a subtle objection: if Gabriel taught the Prophet (Quran 53:5), doesn't that make Gabriel superior? The answer clarifies a vital distinction: Gabriel is a conveyor, not the true teacher. True teaching belongs to Allah alone, so the verse does not imply angelic superiority over prophets.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. The objection quotes Quran 53:5 describing Gabriel as 'severe in power' and argues that the teacher (Gabriel) is better than the student (the Prophet).
Notice how the objection uses a linguistic inference: verb 'taught' implies a subject and object.
2
Study the refutation
The answer (وأجيب) states that Gabriel is a conveyer (مبلغ), not a teacher. The act of teaching is exclusively from Allah. This shifts the focus from Gabriel's role to Allah's role.
The key distinction is between tabligh (conveying) and ta'leem (teaching).
3
Reflect on the implication
Understand why this refutation is effective: even if Gabriel is called a 'teacher' in a broad sense, the true source of knowledge is Allah, so no superiority over the Prophet is established.
This objection is one of several against angelic superiority; each is answered by showing the angel's function is derivative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع - علمه شديد القوى ) (٣) يعني جبريل، والمعلم أفضل . وأجيب بأنه مبلغ، وإنما التعليم من الله .
The fourth: 'Taught him one of severe powers' (53:5), meaning Gabriel, and the teacher is better. And it was answered that he is a conveyer, and teaching is only from God.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth objection for angels' superiority, using the verse that describes Gabriel as the teacher of the Prophet. The objection claims that the teacher (Gabriel) is superior to the student (the Prophet). The answer (وأجيب) refutes this by stating that Gabriel is merely a conveyer (مبلغ) of revelation, and the true teacher is God. Thus, the verse does not imply superiority of Gabriel over the Prophet.

Key Terms
جبريل
المعلم
المبلغ
التعليم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Because Gabriel is called a 'teacher' in the Quran (53:5), he is superior to the Prophet.
Correction: Gabriel is a conveyer, not the true teacher; the act of teaching belongs to Allah, so the verse does not imply Gabriel's superiority.

Checkpoint
How does the answer refute the claim that Gabriel is superior because he taught the Prophet?
A) Gabriel is not a teacher but a conveyer.
B) The Prophet is superior because he learned.
C) The verse is not authentic.
D) Angels are not teachers.

Key Takeaway
The fourth objection is refuted by showing Gabriel is a conveyer, not the teacher; true teaching is from Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you learn something new, do you pause to thank the ultimate Teacher, Allah, or do you only credit the human who taught you?
?
Has your admiration for a teacher, scholar, or even an angel ever led you to forget that all knowledge is from Allah? How can you realign your heart?
?
If you are a teacher or convey knowledge to others, do you ever feel a sense of pride as if you are the source? How does this passage remind you of your true role?

The Fifth Objection from the Verse 'Lan Yastankifa' and Its Refutation
Objection and refutation using the verse 'Lan Yastankifa'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic argument behind the fifth objection for angels' superiority and how the refutation clarifies the verse's true meaning regarding specific attributes.

Core Idea
The verse's phrasing does not prove angelic superiority; it highlights specific attributes.

In this lesson, we examine the fifth objection for the superiority of angels over prophets, based on the Qur'anic verse that mentions angels after Christ. The objection uses Arabic linguistic conventions to claim a hierarchy. The refutation clarifies the true meaning, showing that the verse is about specific traits rather than overall rank.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and the objection
Understand how the Arabic phrasing 'lan yastankifa ... wa-la ...' is used to imply that angels are above Christ.
The verse is 4:172.
2
Identify the linguistic argument
Recognize the principle that saying 'neither X nor Y' often places Y higher.
3
Study the refutation
Notice the response that the expression indicates increase in the cause of disdain, such as Christ's unique birth and miracles, and angels' lack of parents and greater powers.
The refutation is introduced with 'وأجيب'.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Consider how this refutation defends the high status of prophets despite the apparent wording.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامس - لن يستنكف المسيح أن يكون عبد ا لله ولا الملائكة المقربون فإنه يقال : لا يترفع عن هذا الأمر الأمير ولا من فوقه. ولا يقال : ولا من هو دونه . وأجيب بأن مثله إنما يفيد الزيادة فيما جعل سبباً للترفع والاستنكاف، ككون عيسى عليه السلام) ولد بلا أب وأبرأ الأكمه والأبرص. فالمعنى ولا من هو فوقه الملائكة الذين لا أب لهم ولا أم، ويقدرون على ما لا يقدر عليه عيسى (عليه السلام) في ذلك .
The fifth: 'The Messiah would never disdain to be a servant of God, nor the angels brought near' (4:172). For it is said: 'Neither the prince nor the one above him disdains this matter.' And it is not said: 'Nor the one beneath him.' And it was answered that such an expression only indicates increase in what causes disdain, like Jesus (peace be upon him) being born without a father and healing the blind and the leper. So the meaning is: nor the one above him, i.e., the angels who have no father or mother, and have power over what Jesus (peace be upon him) does not have power over in that regard.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage contains the fifth objection for angels' superiority, based on the verse that mentions angels after Christ. The objection argues that in Arabic, when saying 'neither X nor Y', Y is usually greater, implying angels are above Christ. The answer (وأجيب) explains that the expression can indicate that both are equal in disdain, or that it highlights the specific reasons for potential disdain—Christ's unique birth and miracles, and angels' lack of parents and greater powers. Thus, it does not prove superiority of angels over Christ in all aspects.

Key Terms
المسيح
الملائكة المقربون
الاستنكاف
عيسى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'Lan yastankifa...' proves that angels are superior to prophets in all aspects.
Correction: The refutation shows it only indicates superiority in specific attributes, such as lack of parents and greater powers, not overall rank.

Checkpoint
What does the answer say the verse actually indicates about angels and Christ?
A) Angels are superior in all aspects.
B) They are equal in not disdaining worship.
C) Angels are superior in certain specific attributes like having no parents.
D) Christ is superior.

Key Takeaway
The verse highlights specific attributes that make disdain less likely, not a general hierarchy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read Quranic verses, do you sometimes jump to conclusions based on your own understanding of Arabic? How does this lesson's careful analysis challenge you to seek deeper knowledge before forming beliefs?
?
Consider your own relationships: Have you ever felt inferior or superior to others based on outward attributes? How does the lesson’s focus on specific causes (not general rank) reshape how you view yourself and others in light of Allah’s creation?
?
The refutation uses a specific case: Jesus’ unique birth and powers. How does recognizing that every being has unique attributes help you avoid pride or despair? What attribute do you have that might make you 'above' or 'below' others, and how should you view it after this lesson?

Sixth Objection: The Consistent Mention of Angels Before Prophets
Objection that angels are consistently named before prophets, with refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the consistent mention of angels before prophets does not necessarily indicate their superiority, and the two explanations given by scholars.

Core Idea
Order of mention does not always reflect rank.

In this lesson, we examine the sixth objection against the superiority of angels: that they are consistently named before prophets in the Quran. The answer provides two plausible reasons that preserve the prophets' status. Let's explore the argument and its refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage is very concise.
2
Identify the objection
The objection is that angels are always mentioned before prophets, implying their superiority. Find the phrase that states this.
3
Understand the two answers
The answer gives two reasons: chronological precedence (angels were created before prophets) and the strength of faith required because angels are hidden. Consider each reason.
Both reasons show that order of mention does not necessarily indicate rank.
4
Reflect on the logic
Ask yourself: could there be other reasons? Why does this matter for the debate about angels vs. prophets?
This connects to the broader discussion of which is superior.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السادس - اطراد تقديم ذكرهم على ذكر الأنبياء. وأجيب بأنه لتقدمهم في الوجود، او في قوة الإيمان بهم لخفاء امرهم .
The sixth: The consistent precedence of mentioning them over the mention of prophets. And it was answered that it is due to their precedence in existence, or to the strength of faith in them due to the hidden nature of their affair.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage contains the sixth objection, arguing that because angels are always mentioned before prophets in the Quran, they are superior. The answer (وأجيب) gives two possible reasons: either chronological precedence (angels were created before prophets) or the fact that faith in angels requires more strength because they are hidden from sight. Thus, the order does not necessarily imply superiority in rank.

Key Terms
تقديم
الوجود
الإيمان
الخفاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The consistent mention of angels before prophets proves they are superior in rank.
Correction: The order can be explained by chronological precedence or the strength of faith required, not necessarily rank.

Checkpoint
What are the two reasons given for the consistent precedence of angels' mention?
A) They are more numerous and more powerful.
B) They existed earlier or require stronger faith due to being hidden.
C) They are more beloved to God and have greater knowledge.
D) The prophets requested this order.

Key Takeaway
The order of mention in the Quran does not automatically indicate superiority; contextual reasons like existence and faith strength must be considered.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The objection shows a human bias toward visible order. Where in your relationships or duties have you prioritized what appears first (e.g., in your schedule or attention) over what may be more significant but less apparent? What will you reorder today based on this lesson?

The Seventh Objection: Angels as Pure Spiritual Beings
Objection and refutation regarding angels' nature

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the seventh objection describes angels' perfections and how it is refuted by distinguishing philosophical assumptions from shared and contested claims.

Core Idea
Angels' spiritual perfections do not prove superiority over prophets.

The seventh objection against the superiority of prophets over angels portrays angels as immaterial, perfect, and powerful beings. The response, however, shows that this description rests on unproven philosophical grounds, shared human traits, and contested interpretations. Let's examine the objection and its three-pronged refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the objection and its refutation come through.
Notice the concise style of the refutation.
2
Identify the attributes of angels
List the attributes claimed for angels in the objection: immaterial essence, attachment to celestial structures, freedom from matter and evil, perfections, strength, knowledge of unseen, precedence in good deeds.
These are all presented as self-evident qualities.
3
Understand the three-part refutation
The answer categorizes these attributes into three types: some are based on philosophical principles, some are shared with humans, and some are contested. Notice how this undercuts the claim of angelic uniqueness.
Each category weakens the objection differently.
4
Reflect on the implication
Ask yourself: if some attributes rely on philosophy, are they universally accepted? If some are shared, do they demonstrate superiority? If contested, can they be used as proof?
This leads to the conclusion that the objection fails.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السابع - أنها مجردة في ذواتها متعلقة بالهياكل العلوية مبرأة عن المادة وعن الشرور والقبائح متصفة بالكمالات العلمية والعملية بالعقل، قوية على الأفعال العجيبة، مطلعة على أسرار الغيب سابقة إلى أنواع الخيرات . وأجيب بأن بعضها على قواعد الفلسفة، وبعضها مشترك وبعضها معارض .
The seventh: That they are immaterial in their essences, attached to the celestial structures, free from matter and from evils and abominations, described with intellectual and practical perfections through reason, strong for wondrous acts, informed of the secrets of the unseen, preceding to types of good deeds. And it was answered that some of these [attributes] are based on philosophical principles, some are shared [with humans], and some are contested.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh objection, which describes angels as pure spirits with many perfections, implying their superiority. The answer (وأجيب) responds that these attributes are not all valid: some are based on Greek philosophy, some are shared with humans, and some are contested in their interpretation. Thus, the objection does not prove superiority over prophets.

Key Terms
مجردة
الهياكل العلوية
المادة
الفلسفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Angels are superior to prophets because they are purely spiritual and free from matter.
Correction: The attributes listed either rely on philosophical assumptions, are shared with humans, or are contested in their interpretation, so they do not establish superiority.

Checkpoint

A) They are all true but irrelevant.
B) Some are based on philosophy, some are shared with humans, some are disputed.
C) They are all false.
D) They apply only to certain angels.

Key Takeaway
The seventh objection fails because its supporting attributes are not universally valid: they are either philosophical, shared, or contested.

The Eighth Objection: Angels' Superior Deeds vs. Prophets' Hardships
Objection and answer regarding the superiority of angels' deeds and knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why facing hardships and suppressing desires makes prophets more deserving of reward than angels, despite angels' greater deeds and knowledge.

Core Idea
Hardships and self-struggle earn greater reward than abundant perfect deeds.

This lesson presents the eighth objection against prophethood, arguing that angels perform more numerous, enduring, and perfect deeds, and have superior knowledge. How then can prophets be superior? The answer reveals a key principle: reward is tied to the effort of overcoming opposition and bearing hardships, not merely to the quantity or quality of deeds. This shifts the focus from external performance to internal struggle.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage once. Notice that the objection lists four qualities of angels' deeds and knowledge: more numerous, more enduring, more upright, more complete and abundant.
This is the eighth objection in a series.
2
Understand the answer's principle
The answer begins with "وأجيب" (and it was answered). It introduces a new criterion: being accompanied by suppression of the opposing self and bearing hardships makes one more deserving of reward.
Key Arabic terms: قهر المضاد (suppression of the opposing [self]) and تحمل المشاق (bearing hardships).
3
Connect to the broader argument
Reflect on how this principle defends prophethood: prophets face internal and external struggles that angels do not, so their reward and rank are higher despite outward appearances.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثامن - أن أعمالهم أكثر وأدوم وأقوم، وعلومهم أكمل وأكثر. وأجيب بأن المقرون بقهر المضاد وتحمل المشاق أدخل في استحقاق الثواب .
The eighth: That their deeds are more numerous, more enduring, and more upright, and their knowledge is more complete and more abundant. And it was answered that the one accompanied by suppression of the opposing [self] and bearing hardships is more deserving of reward.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage contains the eighth objection, arguing that angels perform more worship, continuously, with perfect knowledge, making them superior. The answer (وأجيب) counters that prophets face opposition and hardships, which makes them more deserving of reward. Thus, quantity and perfection of deeds do not necessarily indicate superiority without considering context.

Key Terms
الأعمال
العلوم
الثواب
المشاق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that abundant deeds automatically imply a higher rank.
Correction: The answer emphasizes that hardship and struggle against the self increase reward, so prophets can be superior despite fewer or less perfect deeds.

Checkpoint
Why does the answer say prophets may be superior despite fewer deeds?
A) Their deeds are more perfect.
B) They face hardships and suppress their desires, earning more reward.
C) Angels have no free will.
D) Prophets are chosen by God.

Key Takeaway
The key principle: reward is based on the effort of overcoming opposition and bearing hardships, not merely on the quantity or perfection of deeds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform acts of worship, do you seek ease or embrace difficulty? How does this lesson challenge your desire for a comfortable religious life?
?
The objectors thought quantity of deeds matters; what 'quantities' do you rely on to feel righteous? Are you willing to let go of that and embrace the struggle against your own self?
?
Think of a hardship you face for Allah's sake—whether in your prayer, your character, or your daily life. How does this lesson change your perspective on its value and the reward it brings?

Angels' Humility in Prostration (Quran 16:49-50)
Transmitted proof from Quran 16:49-50.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Quran 16:49-50 highlights angels' humility as a transmitted proof for their superiority.

Core Idea
Angels prostrate without arrogance, showing their unique humility.

The first transmitted proof from the Quran describes angels' prostration to God, emphasizing their lack of arrogance and their constant fear of their Lord. This verse is used to argue that angels possess a special humility that others lack, indicating their high station.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and commentary
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note how the commentator extracts specific qualities from the verse.
The verse explicitly mentions prostration, lack of arrogance, fear, and obedience.
2
Identify the described virtues
List the virtues attributed to angels in this verse: humility in prostration, no arrogance, fear of God, obedience, avoidance of prohibitions.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider why these virtues are presented as evidence of angels' superiority. How does contrasting them with others strengthen the argument?
The commentator notes that the verse implies others are not like that.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ايضاً بوجوه نقلية وعقلية، أما النقليات فمنها قوله تعالى: ﴿ والله يسجد ما في السموات وما في الأرض من دابة والملائكة وهم لايستكبرون . يخافون ربهم من فوقهم ويفعلون ما يؤمرون ﴾ خصصهم بالتواضع، وترك الاستكبار في السجود. وفيه إشارة إلى أن غيرهم ليس كذلك، وأن أسباب التكبر والتعظم حاصلة لهم، ووصفهم باستمرار الخوف وامتثال الأوامر ومن جملتها اجتناب المنهيات . ومنها قوله تعالى : " ومن عنده لا يستكبرون عن عبادته ولايستحسرون . يسبحون الليل والنهار لا يفترون) (۲) وصفهم بالقرب والشرف عنده وبالتواضع والمواظبة على الطاعة والتسبيح . ومنها قوله تعالى : وبَلْ عباد مكرمون لا يسبقونه بالقول وهم بأمره يعملون ) (۳) .. إلى أن قال: وهم من خشيته مشفقون. وخصهم بالكرامة المطلقة والامتثال والخشية وهذه الأمور أساس كافة الخيرات .
Also with transmitted and rational proofs. As for the transmitted ones, among them is His saying, exalted: 'And to God prostrates whatever is in the heavens and whatever is on the earth of creatures, and the angels, and they are not arrogant. They do not precede Him in speech, and they act by His command' (21:26-27)... until He said: 'And they are in awe of Him' (21:28). And He singled them out with absolute honor, obedience, and fear, and these matters are the foundation of all good things.

Commentary
This passage presents additional transmitted proofs (آيضاً بوجوه نقلية) for the superiority of angels. It cites three Quranic verses that describe angels' humility, continuous worship, obedience, and fear of God. The commentary on each verse highlights that God singles out angels for these virtues, implying they are superior to other beings, including prophets. The proofs are meant to support the claim that angels are better than humans. The passage ends before any answer is given, as it is incomplete in this window.

Angels worship tirelessly, showing their superior devotion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ايضاً بوجوه نقلية وعقلية، أما النقليات فمنها قوله تعالى: ﴿ والله يسجد ما في السموات وما في الأرض من دابة والملائكة وهم لايستكبرون . يخافون ربهم من فوقهم ويفعلون ما يؤمرون ﴾ خصصهم بالتواضع، وترك الاستكبار في السجود. وفيه إشارة إلى أن غيرهم ليس كذلك، وأن أسباب التكبر والتعظم حاصلة لهم، ووصفهم باستمرار الخوف وامتثال الأوامر ومن جملتها اجتناب المنهيات . ومنها قوله تعالى : " ومن عنده لا يستكبرون عن عبادته ولايستحسرون . يسبحون الليل والنهار لا يفترون) (۲) وصفهم بالقرب والشرف عنده وبالتواضع والمواظبة على الطاعة والتسبيح . ومنها قوله تعالى : وبَلْ عباد مكرمون لا يسبقونه بالقول وهم بأمره يعملون ) (۳) .. إلى أن قال: وهم من خشيته مشفقون. وخصهم بالكرامة المطلقة والامتثال والخشية وهذه الأمور أساس كافة الخيرات .
Also with transmitted and rational proofs. As for the transmitted ones, among them is His saying, exalted: 'And to God prostrates whatever is in the heavens and whatever is on the earth of creatures, and the angels, and they are not arrogant. They fear their Lord above them and do what they are commanded' (16:49-50). He specified them with humility and abandoning arrogance in prostration. And in it is an indication that others are not like that, and that causes of pride and haughtiness are present for them, and described them with continuous fear and compliance with commands, including avoidance of prohibitions. And among them is His saying, exalted: 'And those who are near to Him are not arrogant in worship of Him, nor do they become weary. They glorify [Him] night and day, never flagging' (21:19-20). He described them with nearness and honor with Him, and with humility, persistence in obedience and glorification. And among them is His saying, exalted: 'But they are honored servants. They do not precede Him in speech, and they act by His command' (21:26-27)... until He said: 'And they are in awe of Him' (21:28). And He singled them out with absolute honor, obedience, and fear, and these matters are the foundation of all good things.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage presents additional transmitted proofs (آيضاً بوجوه نقلية) for the superiority of angels. It cites three Quranic verses that describe angels' humility, continuous worship, obedience, and fear of God. The commentary on each verse highlights that God singles out angels for these virtues, implying they are superior to other beings, including prophets. The proofs are meant to support the claim that angels are better than humans. The passage ends before any answer is given, as it is incomplete in this window.

?

?

?
The angels glorify God night and day, never flagging. Are there moments in your day when you forget to glorify Him? What change can you make to ensure your day is filled with constant remembrance?

Angels as Honored Servants (Quran 21:26-28)
Transmitted proof from Quran 21:26-28.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Quran 21:26-28 establishes angels' honor, obedience, and fear as proof of their superiority.

Core Idea
Angels are honored servants who always obey and fear God.

The third transmitted proof from the Quran describes angels as 'honored servants' who do not speak before God, act only by His command, and are in awe of Him. These qualities are presented as the foundation of all good things and evidence of their high status.

Guided Path
1

The verse includes 'they are in awe of Him'.
2
Identify the specific honors
List: absolute honor (كرامة مطلقة), obedience (امتثال), and fear (خشية). The commentator calls these the foundation of all good.
3
Reflect on the argument
Consider why these qualities are considered proofs of superiority. How does being 'honored servants' imply a special rank?
The word 'مكرمون' suggests they are honored by God.

Defining Sorcery: Its Nature and Characteristics
Al-Taftazani defines sorcery and lists its essential characteristics.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise definition of sorcery (السحر) as an extraordinary act with specific characteristics, including its teachability and the role of the soul's malice.

Core Idea
Sorcery is an extraordinary act that can be taught and opposed.

Al-Taftazani begins by defining sorcery in technical terms. This is not merely magic or illusion, but a real phenomenon with specific features: it involves performing specific actions, is learnable, fueled by evil intent, and can be counteracted. Understanding this definition is crucial before discussing its permissibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition carefully
Read the Arabic passage where al-Taftazani defines sorcery. Notice the key terms used.
The definition is compact; each phrase carries weight.
2
Identify the four characteristics
List the characteristics mentioned: extraordinary matter, specific actions, teaching/learning, evil motivation, and possible opposition.
These are the essential features that distinguish sorcery from other extraordinary events.
3
Reflect on the term 'kharq al-‘adah'
Understand that sorcery is a 'break in natural law', similar to miracles but with different source and purpose.
This sets the stage for the discussion on permissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : المبحث التاسع - السحر
إظهار أمر خارق للعادة بمباشرة أعمال مخصوصة ، يجري فيها التعليم والتعلم، وتعين عليها شرة النفس وتتأتى فيها المعارضة ، وهو جائز عقلاً كالكرامة والم
المعجزة ، وثابت سمعاً بقوله تعالى : ( يعلمون الناس السحر . . ) الآية . ولما ثبت من أنه سحر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وعائشة ، وابن عمر (رضي الله عنهما) ، والطعن الكاذب من الكفرة في النبي بأنه مسحور أريد به زوال العقل بالسحر، والعصمة المشار إليها بقوله تعالى : والله يعصمك من الناس (٢) العصمة أن يهلكوه، أو يوقعوا خللاً في نبوته . وليس للساحر أن يفعل ما يشاء من الإضرار بالأنبياء، وإزالة ملك الخلفاء وغير ذلك .
He said: The ninth investigation – sorcery. It is the manifestation of an extraordinary matter through specific actions, in which teaching and learning occur, supported by the evilness of the soul, and in which opposition is possible. It is permissible by reason like the karamah and the miracle, and established by scripture by His saying: 'They teach people sorcery...' the verse. And due to what is established that the Prophet (peace be upon him), Aisha, and Ibn Umar (may God be pleased with them) were bewitched, and the false accusation of the disbelievers against the Prophet that he was bewitched, intending by it loss of intellect through sorcery. And the protection indicated by His saying: 'And God will protect you from the people' (2) – the protection is that they kill him or cause a flaw in his prophethood. And the sorcerer cannot do whatever he wishes of harm to the prophets, removal of the rule of the caliphs, and other things.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage defines sorcery (السحر) and affirms its permissibility by both reason and revelation. It begins by stating that sorcery is the manifestation of an extraordinary matter through specific actions that involve teaching and learning, motivated by the evilness of the soul, and can be opposed. It is rationally permissible, like the karamah (miracle of a saint) and the mu'jizah (miracle of a prophet), and scripturally established by the verse 'They teach people sorcery' (Quran 2:102). The author then notes that the Prophet, Aisha, and Ibn Umar were affected by sorcery, and that the disbelievers falsely accused the Prophet of being bewitched to imply loss of intellect. God's protection (عصمة) of the Prophet means that sorcery cannot kill him or cause a decisive flaw in his prophethood. Thus, the sorcerer cannot harm prophets or caliphs as he wishes, because God prevents it.

Key Terms
سحر
خارق للعادة
تعليم
تعلم
شرة النفس
معارضة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a characteristic of sorcery according to the passage?
A) It is an extraordinary matter
B) It involves specific actions
C) It cannot be opposed
D) It is motivated by evil of the soul

Key Takeaway
Sorcery is defined as an extraordinary act that is learnable, motivated by evil, and can be opposed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage says sorcery is driven by 'شرة النفس' (evilness of the soul). When you feel anger or malice towards someone, do you ever feed that feeling instead of suppressing it? What will you do tomorrow to purify your soul from such evil inclinations?
?
Sorcery is defined as a real, learnable skill. Have you ever underestimated the reality of spiritual evil? How does this knowledge change your daily habits of seeking protection through Quran and du'a? Write one specific action you will commit to starting today.
?
The definition includes that sorcery can be opposed. When you see falsehood or injustice around you, do you passively complain or actively confront it with truth? What is one area of your life where you need to stand up and oppose evil, relying on Allah?

The Permissibility of Sorcery: Reason and Revelation
Al-Taftazani presents rational and scriptural evidence for sorcery's permissibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Taftazani proves the rational and scriptural permissibility of sorcery, using analogy to miracles and Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
Sorcery is permissible by reason like miracles, and established by revelation.

Having defined sorcery, al-Taftazani now affirms its permissibility. Rationally, it is similar to miracles (mu'jizah) and saintly wonders (karamah), which are also extraordinary acts. Scripturally, the Quran mentions people teaching sorcery, implying its reality and permissibility. Moreover, historical incidents of the Prophet and his companions being affected by sorcery further confirm its existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the rational proof
Al-Taftazani states that sorcery is rationally permissible like karamah and mu'jizah. Reflect on why analogy works.
All three are extraordinary; the difference lies in source and purpose.
2
Read the scriptural proof
He quotes the Quranic verse 'They teach people sorcery' as evidence. Understand that the Quran acknowledges sorcery without condemning its existence.
The verse implies that sorcery is a real practice that can be taught.
3
Consider the historical examples
The Prophet, Aisha, and Ibn Umar were affected by sorcery. This shows that sorcery has real effects.
These incidents are from authentic hadith, confirming sorcery's reality.

?

Repent sincerely if your motives have been impure, and resolve to only seek beneficial knowledge that increases taqwa.

Limitations of Sorcery: Divine Protection of Prophets
Al-Taftazani refutes the claim of sorcery affecting prophets and asserts divine protection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic doctrine of 'isma (protection) and its limitation on sorcery's effect on prophets and leaders.

Core Idea
Sorcery cannot harm prophets or caliphs as it wishes; God protects them.

Despite sorcery's reality and permissibility, its power is not absolute. Al-Taftazani addresses the false accusation that the Prophet was bewitched (implying loss of intellect) and clarifies that divine protection (عصمة) prevents sorcery from killing prophets or undermining their prophethood. This lesson explores the limits of sorcery and the doctrine of prophetic immunity.

Guided Path
1
Examine the false accusation
Al-Taftazani mentions that disbelievers falsely accused the Prophet of being bewitched, implying his intellect was affected.
This is a slander that contradicts the 'isma of prophets.
2
Understand the concept of 'isma
The verse 'And God will protect you from the people' indicates that God protects the Prophet from being killed or having his prophethood flawed.
'Isma means preservation from mortal harm and from anything that would undermine his message.
3
Note the practical limitation
Sorcerers cannot arbitrarily harm prophets or caliphs. Their power is constrained by God's will.
This refutes the idea that sorcery can overthrow rulers at will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt that someone's harm—whether through envy, magic, or oppression—could irreversibly destroy your faith or life? How does the truth that God's protection (عصمة) limits all harm change the way you view your deepest fears? Will you today surrender that fear to God alone?
?
When you hear a slanderous accusation against a religious leader or someone you respect, do you automatically assume it might be true? This passage teaches that even the Prophet was falsely accused by disbelievers. What does this demand of you in how you evaluate accusations? Are you willing to be slow to believe and quick to seek evidence?
?
The passage states that sorcerers cannot do whatever they wish. Is there any person or force in your life that you have given 'unlimited power' to in your mind—as if they can harm you regardless of God's will? How can you actively remind yourself of the limits stated in this passage, starting today?

Refuting the Mu'tazila on Sorcery and the Evil Eye
Al-Taftazani refutes Mu'tazila view on sorcery and affirms the evil eye.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position that the Quranic verse on sorcery does not prove all sorcery is illusion, and that the evil eye is a real phenomenon.

Core Idea
The Quranic verse does not universalize sorcery as illusion; the evil eye is empirically and scripturally affirmed.

Al-Taftazani addresses two related issues: the nature of sorcery and the reality of the evil eye. He refutes the Mu'tazila claim that all sorcery is illusory by clarifying that the Quranic verse (20:66) only describes a specific event, not a universal rule. He then affirms the evil eye as a well-known phenomenon supported by Quran 68:51, and notes that scholars differ on subsidiary practices like incantations and amulets.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the source text carefully, noting key terms like تخييل, تمويه, شعوذة, عين.
The passage is dense; read slowly.
2
Understand the Mu'tazila position
Recognize that the Mu'tazila claim all sorcery is mere illusion and deception, comparable to juggling.
3
Examine the refutation
Al-Taftazani argues that the verse 'It appeared to him from their sorcery' does not entail that every instance of sorcery is illusory; it only describes the effect on Moses during that event.
The refutation is based on the specific context of the verse.
4
Affirm the evil eye
The evil eye is treated as nearly empirically established, and it is supported by the verse 'would almost make you slip with their eyes'.
This shows that supernatural harms are acknowledged in Sunni theology.
5
Note the subsidiary dispute
Scholars who affirm sorcery and the evil eye differ on the permissibility of using incantations, amulets, spitting, and wiping, but these are secondary issues.
This indicates that the main doctrine is agreed upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله تعالى : (يخيل إليه من سحرهم (٣)
لا يدل على أن كل سحر تخييل وتمويه، بمنزلة الشعوذة على ما هو رأي المعتزلة . وأما الإصابة بالعين فتكاد تجري مجرى المشاهدات، وفيها نزل قول وإن يكاد الذين كفروا ليزلقونك بأبصارهم ) (٤)
واختلف القائلون بالسحر والعين في جواز الاستعانة بالرقى والعوذ، وفي جواز تعليق التمائم، والنفث ، والمسح ، والمسألة فرعية).
And His saying: 'It appeared to him from their sorcery' (3) does not indicate that all sorcery is illusion and deception, like juggling, as is the view of the Mu'tazila. As for affliction by the evil eye, it almost runs the course of observed matters, and concerning it was revealed the saying 'And indeed those who disbelieve would almost make you slip with their eyes' (4). And those who affirm sorcery and the evil eye differed regarding the permissibility of seeking aid through incantations and amulets, and regarding the permissibility of hanging talismans, spitting, wiping, and the matter is subsidiary.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage refutes the Mu'tazila position that all sorcery is mere illusion (تخييل وتمويه) like juggling (الشعوذة). The author argues that the verse 'It appeared to him from their sorcery' (Quran 20:66) does not necessitate that every sorcery is purely imaginary. He then discusses the evil eye (العين), stating that it is nearly empirically established as a real phenomenon, and cites the verse 'And indeed those who disbelieve would almost make you slip with their eyes' (Quran 68:51). Finally, he notes that scholars differ on subsidiary rulings such as using incantations (رقى), amulets (تمائم), spitting (نفث), and wiping (مسح), but these are secondary issues.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quranic verse 'It appeared to him from their sorcery' proves that all sorcery is mere illusion and deception.
Correction: The verse describes only what appeared to Moses from the magicians' sorcery; it does not establish a universal rule that all sorcery is illusory, nor does it deny the reality of harmful sorcery.

Checkpoint
What view of the Mu'tazila is refuted in this passage?
A) That sorcery is rationally impossible
B) That all sorcery is mere illusion and deception
C) That sorcery is a type of miracle
D) That the evil eye does not exist

Key Takeaway
The Quranic verse on sorcery does not support the Mu'tazila claim that all sorcery is illusion; the evil eye is a real phenomenon backed by revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that the evil eye can affect you? How does this belief change the way you interact with others, especially when you feel envy or pride? Will you seek protection from it with sincerity, or dismiss it as superstition?
?
Have you ever doubted the reality of the unseen because it seemed irrational? What in your life needs to change to align your heart with what Allah has revealed about sorcery and the evil eye, even if your intellect resists?
?
The Mu'tazila rejected sorcery based on reason. Where in your life do you prioritize your own reasoning over divine revelation? Are you willing to submit to Allah's words even when they challenge your intellect, and what step will you take today to cultivate that submission?

Definition of Sorcery and Its Distinction from Miracles
Al-Taftazani defines sorcery and lists its distinguishing features from miracles and karamah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise definition of sorcery according to Ahl al-Haqq and how it differs from miracles and saintly wonders.

Core Idea
Sorcery is an extraordinary act from an evil soul, distinct in its source, method, and moral condition.

Al-Taftazani begins by defining sorcery precisely, distinguishing it from miracles (mu'jizah) and saintly wonders (karamah). This definition is crucial for understanding its rational and scriptural status. The passage also mentions the Mu'tazila view that sorcery is mere illusion, like juggling.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the definition and distinctions.
Notice the structure: definition, then six points of difference, then the Mu'tazila objection.
2
Identify the six differences
The passage lists six ways sorcery differs from miracles and saintly wonders. Find each one and note the key phrase.
The differences include: source (evil soul), learning required, not on demand, limited conditions, can be opposed, practitioner's immorality.
3
Understand the Mu'tazila view
The Mu'tazila claim sorcery is merely showing what has no reality, like juggling. Compare this to the Ahl al-Haqq definition.
This sets up the need for evidence, which comes in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إظهار أمر خارق للعادة من نفس شريرة خبيثة بمباشرة أعمال مخصوصة يجري فيها التعلم والتتلمذ ، وبهذين الاعتبارين يفارق المعجزة والكرامة، وبأنه لا يكون بحسب اقتراح المقترحين، وبأنه يختص ببعض الأزمنة أو الأمكنة أو الشرائط،
وبانه قد يتصدى بمعارضته ، ويبذل الجهد في الإتيان بمثله ، وبأن صاحبه ربما يعلن بالفسق، ويتصف بالرجس في الظاهر والباطن، والخزي في الدنيا والآخرة .. إلى غير ذلك من وجوه المفارقة وهو عند أهل الحق جائز عقلاً، ثابت سمعاً، وكذلك الإصابة بالعين . وقالت المعتزلة : بل هو مجرد إراءة ما لا حقيقة له بمنزلة الشعبذة التي سببها خفة حركات اليد أو خفاء وجه الحيلة فيه لنا على الجواز ما مر في الإعجاز من إمكان الأمر في نفسه وشمول قدرة الله تعالى، فإنه هو الخالق، وإنما الساحر فاعل وكاسب . وأيضاً إجماع الفقهاء، وإنما اختلفوا في الحكم، وعلى الوقوع وجوه : منها قوله تعالى :
يعلمون الناس السحر وما أنزل على الملكين بابل هاروت وماروت . . إلى قوله فيتعلمون منهما ما يفرقون به بين المرء وزوجه وما هم بضارين به من أحد إلا بإذن الله (١)
وفيه إشعار بأنه ثابت حقيقة ليس مجرد إراءة ،وتمويه وبأن المؤثر والخالق هو الله وحده .
ومنها سورة الفلق، فقد اتفق جمهور المسلمين على أنها نزلت فيما كانت من سحر لبيد بن أعصم اليهودي للرسول الله حتى مرض ثلاث ليال. ومنها ما روي أن جارية سحرت عائشة رضي الله عنها) وأنه سحر ابن عمر (رضي الله عنه فتكوعت يده .
فإن قيل : لو صح السحر الأضرت السحرة بجميع الأنبياء والصالحين، ولحصلوا لأنفسهم الملك العظيم، وكيف يصح أن يسحر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وقد قال الله تعالى : والله يعصمك من الناس (٢) ولا يفلح الساحر حيث أتى (٣)
وكانت الكفرة يعيبون النبي بأنه مسحور، مع القطع بأنهم كاذبون .
The manifestation of an extraordinary matter from an evil, wicked soul through specific actions in which learning and teaching occur. By these two considerations it differs from the miracle and the karamah, and by the fact that it does not occur at the request of those who demand it, and by the fact that it is specific to certain times, places, or conditions, and by the fact that it may be confronted with opposition and effort exerted to produce its like, and by the fact that its practitioner may openly declare immorality and be characterized by filth in appearance and inner self, and disgrace in this world and the Hereafter... to other aspects of difference. And it is, according to the people of truth, rationally permissible and scripturally established, and likewise affliction by the evil eye. The Mu'tazila said: Rather it is merely showing what has no reality, like juggling, the cause of which is lightness of hand movements or concealment of the trick. For us, the proof of its permissibility is what was mentioned in the discussion of miracles regarding the possibility of the matter in itself and the comprehensiveness of God's power, for He is the Creator, and the sorcerer is only an agent and acquirer. Also, the consensus of the jurists, but they differed regarding the ruling. And there are proofs for its occurrence: among them is His saying: 'They teach people sorcery and what was revealed to the two angels at Babylon, Harut and Marut...' up to His saying 'they learn from them that by which they cause separation between a man and his wife, but they do not harm anyone through it except by God's permission' (1). In this there is an indication that it is established in reality, not mere showing and deception, and that the effective agent and creator is God alone. And among them is Surat al-Falaq, for the majority of Muslims agreed that it was revealed concerning the sorcery of Labid ibn A'sam the Jew against the Messenger of God until he fell ill for three nights. And among them is what is narrated that a slave girl bewitched Aisha (may God be pleased with her) and that Ibn Umar (may God be pleased with him) was bewitched so his hand became clenched. If it is said: If sorcery were real, sorcerers would harm all prophets and righteous people, and they would obtain for themselves great kingship, and how can it be correct that the Prophet was bewitched when God said: 'And God will protect you from the people' (2) and 'The sorcerer will not prosper wherever he comes' (3)? And the disbelievers used to criticize the Prophet as being bewitched, while it is certain that they are liars. [Then the answer implied but not explicitly stated: sorcery does not undermine prophethood, God's protection prevents decisive harm, and the sorcerer does not ultimately prosper.]
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage provides the precise definition of sorcery (السحر) from the perspective of Ahl al-Haqq, distinguishing it from miracles (معجزة) and saintly wonders (كرامة). Sorcery originates from an evil soul, involves learning and teaching, is not performed on demand, is limited in time/place/conditions, can be opposed, and its practitioner openly sins and suffers disgrace. Despite its reality, it is permissible by reason and established by scripture. The Mu'tazila claim it is mere illusion (إراءة) like juggling. The author rebuts: sorcery is possible because God is the all-powerful creator; the sorcerer is only an acquirer. Consensus of jurists also supports its reality, though they differ on its ruling. Proofs from scripture include: (1) the verse about Harut and Marut teaching sorcery, which indicates it is real and that harm occurs only by God's permission; (2) Surat al-Falaq, which was revealed due to the Prophet being bewitched by Labid; (3) reports of Aisha and Ibn Umar being bewitched. An objection is then raised: if sorcery is real, why don't sorcerers harm all prophets and seize power? The author implies the answer: God protects prophets from lethal harm, and sorcerers ultimately fail, as per the Quranic verses. The disbelievers' accusation that the Prophet was bewitched is false because sorcery does not negate prophethood.

نفس شريرة
معجزة
كرامة

Checkpoint
According to al-Taftazani's definition, what is the source of sorcery?
A) A pure soul
B) An evil, wicked soul
C) Divine revelation
D) The wind

Key Takeaway
Sorcery is defined as an extraordinary act from an evil soul, learnable and distinct from miracles by six features.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you witness something extraordinary, do you immediately consider its source – is it from Allah, a saint, or an evil soul? How does this passage call you to examine the spiritual origin of wonders in your life?
?
The practitioner of sorcery is characterized by filth in appearance and inner self. Is there any area of your life where you have tolerated moral filth for the sake of some perceived benefit? How will you cleanse it today?
?
The Mu'tazila reduced sorcery to mere trickery. Could it be that you have reduced the supernatural to mere coincidence? What would it mean for your worldview if sorcery and the evil eye are real as the Qur'an says? How must you change your precautions?

Evidence for the Reality of Sorcery and Answering an Objection
Al-Taftazani presents rational and scriptural proofs for sorcery's reality and answers an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational and scriptural proofs for the reality of sorcery and how to answer the objection that it contradicts prophetic protection.

Core Idea
Sorcery is real because God is the sole creator, scripture affirms it, and prophets are ultimately protected.

Having defined sorcery, al-Taftazani now provides evidence for its reality from reason, consensus, and the Quran. He then addresses the objection that if sorcery were real, sorcerers would harm all prophets and seize power. The implied answer is that God's protection prevents fatal harm and sorcerers ultimately fail.

Guided Path
1
Read the rebuttal and evidence section
Read the Arabic passage from 'لنا على الجواز' to the end. Note the three types of proofs: rational, consensus, and scriptural.
The rational proof involves the distinction between Creator and agent. The scriptural proofs include the Harut and Marut verse, Surat al-Falaq, and narrations.
2
Analyze the rational proof
Understand the argument: God is the sole creator (خالق), the sorcerer is only an agent (فاعل) and acquirer (كاسب). Therefore, sorcery is possible under God's power.
This refutes the Mu'tazila claim that sorcery is mere illusion.
3
Examine the scriptural proofs
Identify each proof: the Harut and Marut verse indicates sorcery is real and harm occurs only by God's permission; Surat al-Falaq was revealed because the Prophet was bewitched; the reports about Aisha and Ibn Umar.
These demonstrate that sorcery has real effects.
4
Understand the objection and implied answer
The objection: if sorcery is real, why don't sorcerers harm all prophets and gain power? The implied answer: God protects prophets from fatal harm (عصمة) and sorcerers do not ultimately prosper, as per Quran.
The disbelievers' accusation of the Prophet being bewitched is false because sorcery does not negate prophethood.

?

?

The Reality of the Evil Eye
Establishment of the evil eye's reality with proofs and response to objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the evidence for the reality of the evil eye from Quran and hadith, and how a key objection is answered.

Core Idea
The evil eye is a real harm caused by admiration, confirmed by revelation.

Are physical or spiritual harms caused simply by looking? The Qur'an and Sunnah affirm that some souls have the property of bringing harm when they intensely admire something. This passage from Sharh al-Maqasid establishes the reality of the evil eye with scriptural proofs, and also addresses a rational objection from the Mu'tazili theologian al-Jubba'i. Let's explore the arguments.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition
Read how the author defines the evil eye: a property in some souls that when they admire something, harm befalls it. Note that the author considers this almost as evident as sensory observation.
This definition is crucial for what follows.
2
Examine the hadith proofs
The author cites two hadith: 'The eye is real' and 'The eye brings a man to the grave and a camel to the pot.' Reflect on how these establish the reality of the evil eye.
3
Analyze the Quranic proof
Many exegetes interpret Q 68:51 as referring to the evil eye. The author recounts a story about Banu Asad. Notice how the verse is used as evidence.
This connects the evil eye to the Prophet himself.
4
Consider the objection and answer
Al-Jubba'i argued that the disbelievers looked with hatred, not admiration, so the verse cannot refer to the evil eye. The author answers that they admired the Prophet's eloquence despite hating his religion. Why is this distinction important?
This shows how kalam scholars defend traditional positions against rational objections.
5
Note the differences on practices
The passage ends by mentioning that scholars differ on using incantations, charms, amulets, blowing, and wiping. This indicates that affirming the evil eye does not automatically settle all related rulings.
This is a preview of further discussion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الإصابة بالعين وهو أن يكون لبعض النفوس خاصية أنها إذا استحسنت شيئاً لحقته الآفة، فثبوتها يكاد يجري مجرى المشاهدات التي لا تفتقر إلى حجة . وقد قال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : العين حق . وقال : العين يدخل الرجل القبر، والجمل القدر. وذهب كثير من المفسرين إلى أن قوله تعالى : وإن يكاد الذين كفروا ليزلقونك بأبصارهم . . ) (۲) الآية . نزل في ذلك، وقالوا : كان العين في بني أسد، وكان الرجل منهم يتجوع ثلاثة أيام، فلا يمر به شيء يقول فيه : لم أر كاليوم، إلا عانه ، فالتمس الكفار من بعض من كانت له هذه الصفة ان يقول في رسول الله لذلك فعصمه الله ، واعترض الجبائي بأن القوم ما كانوا ينظرون إلى النبي و نظر استحسان بل مقت و بغض . والجواب : أنهم كانوا يستحسنون منه الفصاحة وكثيراً من الصفات . وإن كانوا يبغضونه من جهة الدين، ثم للقائلين بالسحر والعين إختلاف في جواز الاستعانة بالرقى والعوذ وفي جواز تعليق التمائم، وفي جواز النفث والمسح ، ولكل من
And as for affliction by the evil eye (al-ʿayn), it is that some souls have a property that when they admire something, harm befalls it. Its establishment almost runs in the course of observed matters that do not require a proof. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The eye is real.' And he said: 'The eye brings a man to the grave, and a camel to the pot.' Many exegetes held that His saying: And indeed those who disbelieve would almost make you slip with their eyes... (Q 68:51) was revealed concerning that. They said: The evil eye was among Banu Asad, and a man among them would fast for three days, and nothing passed by him but he would say 'I have not seen the like of today,' and it would be afflicted. So the disbelievers sought from someone who had this quality to say that concerning the Messenger of God, but God protected him. Al-Jubba'i objected that the people did not look at the Prophet with admiration but with hatred and enmity. The answer: They admired his eloquence and many qualities, even though they hated him in terms of religion. Then there is difference among those who affirm sorcery and the eye regarding the permissibility of seeking help with incantations (ruqā) and charms (ʿawadh), and regarding the permissibility of hanging amulets (tamāʾim), and regarding the permissibility of blowing and wiping, and for each...
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage establishes the reality of the evil eye (al-ʿayn) as a genuine phenomenon. The author defines it as a property in some souls that when they admire something, harm follows. He asserts that its reality is almost as certain as observed matters, needing no proof. He then provides two hadith proofs: the Prophet said 'The eye is real' and 'The eye brings a man to the grave and a camel to the pot.' He then cites a Quranic proof: many exegetes interpret Q 68:51 ('And indeed those who disbelieve would almost make you slip with their eyes') as referring to the evil eye. According to them, the Banu Asad tribe were known for this, and the disbelievers tried to use a person with this property against the Prophet, but God protected him. The Mu'tazili theologian al-Jubba'i objected that the disbelievers looked with hatred, not admiration. The author answers that they admired his eloquence and many qualities even while hating his religion. Finally, the author notes that those who affirm sorcery and the eye differ on related practices: the permissibility of using incantations, charms, amulets, blowing, and wiping. The sentence is incomplete at the end of the page.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The evil eye is just superstition and has no basis in Islamic sources.
Correction: The evil eye is affirmed by the Prophet (hadith) and by the interpretation of Quranic verses.

Checkpoint
What was al-Jubba'i's objection regarding the verse 'And indeed those who disbelieve would almost make you slip with their eyes'?
A) He denied that the evil eye exists at all.
B) He argued that the disbelievers looked with hatred, not admiration.
C) He claimed the verse refers to sorcery, not the evil eye.
D) He said the Prophet was immune to the evil eye.

Key Takeaway
The evil eye is a real harm confirmed by hadith and Quran, and scholars have defended it against rational objections.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see someone blessed with something you lack, does your heart feel a sting of envy or a genuine admiration that could inadvertently harm them? How can you train yourself to bless (say 'Mā shāʼ Allāh') before admiration turns into a harmful glance?
?
The Prophet ﷺ was protected from the evil eye of the disbelievers, yet you are not. Do you take the means of protection taught in the Sunnah, like reciting al-Muʿawwidhāt, or do you neglect them out of carelessness?
?
Imagine a friend compliments your new possession and later it breaks. Do you suspect the evil eye, or do you dismiss it as coincidence? If you truly believe the eye is real, what will you change about how you respond to compliments and how you give them?

Unseen Matters
intermediate

The Principle of Possibility and the Ilzam Argument
Al-Taftazani states the claim and gives two proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Taftazani's two foundational arguments for the permissibility of re-creating the non-existent: the principle of possibility (al-imkan) and the compulsion (ilzam) that the return is like the beginning.

Core Idea
The default for all things is possibility until a proof shows otherwise.

Al-Taftazani opens the investigation into re‑creation by establishing that the default rational judgment for any act of God is possibility. He then drives home a powerful ilzam: if the first creation was possible, the second must also be possible because it is the same thing. This lesson unpacks those two arguments and the objection they face.

Guided Path
1
Read the statement of the claim
Start by reading al‑Taftazani's opening sentence: 'It is permissible to re‑create the non‑existent, contrary to the philosophers.' Notice who disagrees and why this is a disputed topic.
The philosophers deny re‑creation absolutely; some Mu'tazila deny it for accidents.
2
Examine the first proof: iqna' (inducement)
The author argues that the original principle (al-asl) is possibility (al‑imkan). Anything not proven necessary or impossible remains possible. The burden of proof falls on the one claiming impossibility.
This is a methodological principle shared even by philosophers.
3
Examine the second proof: ilzam (compulsion)
The return (al‑ma'ad) is exactly the same as the beginning (al‑mabda'). If the first existence was possible, the second cannot be impossible. Times do not affect essential possibility.
This argument targets those who accept the first creation but deny the re‑creation.
4
Consider the objection and the response
An objector might say the thing became impossible due to some necessary condition. Al‑Taftazani responds: either that condition renders it impossible or not; if not, the objection fails. Notice the dialectical style.
The response is cut short in the text but shows the method of engagement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : المبحث الأول - يجوز إعادة المعدوم خلافاً للفلاسفة مطلقاً، ولبعض المعتزلة في الأعراض، ولبعضهم في غير الباقية منها كالأصوات لنا إقناعاً أن الأصل هو الإمكان حتى يقوم دليل الوجوب أو الامتناع، والزاماً أن المعاد مثل المبدأ، بل عينه، فيمتنع كونه ممكناً في وقت ممتنعاً في وقت بل ربما يدعي أن الوجود الأول إفادة زيادة استعداد لقبول الوجود على ما يشير إليه قوله تعالى وهو أهون عليه (1) وفيه نظر لا يقال : لعله امتنع لأمر لازم لأنا نقول فيمتنع أو لا . كثير من مباحث المتكلمين يرى في الظاهر أجنبية عن العلم بالعقائد الدينية، ويعلم عند تحقيق المقاصد الأصلية أنها نافعة في إيراد الحجج عليها، أو دفع الشبه عنها وذلك كإعادة المعدوم، وثبوت الجزء ،والخلاء، وصحة الفناء على العالم، وجواز الخرق على الأفلاك، وعدم اشتراط الحياة بالبنية، وعدم لزوم تناهي القوى الجسمانية ، ونحو ذلك في إثبات الحشر وعذاب القبر، والخلود في الجنة أو النار .. وغير ذلك على اختلاف الآراء وإنما أخر بحث إعادة المعدوم خاصة إلى ههنا لما لها من زيادة الاختصاص بأمر المعاد حيث لا يفتقر إليها إلا في إثبات المعاد بطريق الوجود بعد الفناء اتفق جمهور المتكلمين على جوازها والحكماء على امتناعها وأما المعتزلة فذهب غير البصري إلى جواز إعادة الجواهر، لكن بناء على بقاء ذواتها في العدم، حتى لو بطلت لاستحالت إعادتها، واختلفوا في الاعراض ، فقال بعضهم : يمتنع إعادتها مطلقاً، لأن المعاد إنما يعاد بمعنى فيلزم قيام المعنى بالمعنى . وإلى هذا ذهب بعض أصحابنا . وقال الأكثرون منهم بامتناع إعادة الاعراض التي لا تبقى كالأصوات والإرادات لاختصاصها عندهم بالأوقات، وقسموا الباقية الى ما يكون مقدوراً للعبد، وحكموا بأنه لا يجوز إعادتها، لا للعبد ولا للرب، وإلى ما لا يكون مقدوراً للعبد، وجوزوا إعادتها لنا إقناعاً أن الأصل فيما لا دليل على وجوبه وامتناعه هو الإمكان على ما قالت الحكماء أن كل ما قرع سمعك من الغرائب فذره في بقعة الامكان ما لم يزدك قائم البرهان. فمن ادعى عدم إعادة المعدوم فعليه الدليل، وإلزاماً أن المعاد مثل المبدأ، بل عينه لأن الكلام في إعادة المعدوم بعينه، ويستحيل كون الشيء ممكناً في وقت ممتنعاً في وقت للقطع بأنه لا أثر للأوقات فيما هو بالذات . وعلى هذا لا يرد ما يقال أن العود ، وهو الوجود ثانياً أخص من مطلق الوجود، ولا يلزم من إمكان الأعم إمكان الأخص. وقريب من هذا ما يقال أن المعدوم الممكن قابل للوجود ضرورة استحالة الانقلاب فالوجود الأول أن إفادة زيادة استعداد لقبول الوجود على ما هو شأن سائر القوابل، بناء على اكتساب ملكة الاتصاف بالفعل، فقد صار قابليته للوجود ثانياً أقرب وإعادته على الفاعل أهون، ويشبه أن يكون هذا هو الحق. والمراد بقوله تعالى : وهو الذي يبدأ الخلق ثم يعيده وهو أهون عليه ) (۱) وإن لم يفده زيادة الاستعداد فمعلوم بالضرورة أنه لا عليه بالذات من قابلية الوجود في جميع الأوقات. هذا ولكن الأقرب أن تحمل الإعادة التي جعلت أهون على إعادة الأجزاء ومـا تفتت من المواد إلى ما كانت عليه من الصور والتأليفات على ما يشير إليه قوله تعالى : قل يحييها الذي أنشأها أول مرة ) (۲) لا على إعادة المعدوم، لأنه لم يبق
He said: The First Investigation – It is permissible to re-create the non-existent, contrary to the philosophers absolutely, and contrary to some Mu'tazila regarding accidents, and contrary to some of them regarding what does not remain among them, like sounds. For us, as an inducement (iqna'an), [we say] that the original principle is possibility (al-imkan) until a proof of necessity or impossibility arises, and as a compulsion (ilzaman) that the return (al-ma'ad) is like the beginning (al-mabda'), nay, it is the very same thing, so it is impossible for it to be possible at one time and impossible at another time. Rather, perhaps it is claimed that the first existence confers an increase of preparedness for receiving existence, as indicated by His saying, exalted is He, 'and it is easier for Him' (wa huwa ahwanu 'alayhi) – and there is a consideration in this. It cannot be said: perhaps it is impossible due to a necessary matter, for we say: either it is impossible or not. Many of the investigations of the theologians seem outwardly alien to the knowledge of religious beliefs, but when the original objectives are verified, it is known that they are beneficial in presenting proofs for them or repelling doubts about them. That includes re-creating the non‑existent, the subsistence of the atom, the void, the validity of annihilation for the world, the permissibility of breaking through the celestial spheres, the non‑conditionality of life by the body, the non‑necessity of the finitude of physical powers, and the like, in proving the Resurrection, the punishment of the grave, and eternal life in Paradise or Hell… and other things according to the diversity of opinions. He only delayed the discussion of re‑creating the non‑existent specifically to this place because of its special relevance to the matter of the Return (al‑ma'ad), since it is not needed except in proving the Return by way of existence after annihilation. The majority of theologians agreed on its permissibility, and the philosophers on its impossibility. As for the Mu'tazila, Basran sect held the permissibility of re‑creating substances, but based on the persistence of their essences in non‑existence, so that if they were annihilated, their re‑creation would be impossible. They differed regarding accidents. Some of them said: their re‑creation is absolutely impossible because the re‑created thing (al-mu'ad) is only re‑created by a meaning (bi-ma'nan), so it would entail the subsistence of a meaning by a meaning. Some of our companions (Ash'aris) held this view. The majority of them said: it is impossible to re‑create those accidents that do not persist, like sounds and wills, due to their specificity to times according to them. They divided the persisting accidents into what is within the ability of the servant, and ruled that it is not permissible to re‑create them, neither for the servant nor for the Lord; and into what is not within the ability of the servant, and they permitted its re‑creation. For us, as an inducement (iqna'an), [we say] that the original principle regarding what there is no proof of its necessity or impossibility is possibility (al-imkan), as the philosophers said: 'Whatever strange thing reaches your ears, cast it into the realm of possibility as long as a clear proof does not prevent you.' So whoever claims the impossibility of re‑creating the non‑existent, the burden of proof is on him. And as a compulsion (ilzaman), that the return (al-ma'ad) is like the beginning (al-mabda'), nay, it is the very same thing, because the discussion is about re‑creating the very same non‑existent. It is impossible for a thing to be possible at one time and impossible at another, because it is certain that times have no effect on what is in itself [possible]. On this basis, what is said – that the return (al-'awd), which is existence a second time, is more specific than absolute existence, and the possibility of the more general does not entail the possibility of the more specific – is not valid. Close to this is what is said: the non‑existent possible is receptive to existence by the necessity of the impossibility of conversion; the first existence confers an increase of preparedness for receiving existence, as is the case of all recipients, based on acquiring a disposition for being qualified by the act. So its receptivity for existence a second time becomes closer, and its re‑creation is easier for the Agent. And this seems to be the truth. What is meant by His saying, exalted is He: 'It is He who begins creation, then repeats it, and it is easier for Him' (al‑Rum 30:27) – even if it does not confer an increase of preparedness, yet it is known necessarily that there is no inherent impossibility in its receptivity to existence at all times. But the closest [interpretation] is to carry the re‑creation that is made easier upon the re‑creation of the parts and what has become disintegrated from the materials into what they were of forms and structures, as indicated by His saying, exalted is He: 'Say: He will give them life who created them the first time' (Ya Sin 36:79), not upon re‑creating the non‑existent, because it has not remained.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage presents the first investigation (al-mabhas al-awwal) of the chapter on al-ma'ad, concerning the permissibility of re-creating the non-existent (i'adat al-ma'dum). The author begins by stating the position that it is permissible, contrary to the philosophers who deny it absolutely, and contrary to some Mu'tazila who restrict the denial to accidents or to non‑persistent accidents like sounds. He then gives two arguments: first, an inducement (iqna') that the default judgment for anything is possibility (al-imkan) until a proof establishes necessity or impossibility; second, a compulsion (ilzam) that the return (al-ma'ad) is like the beginning (al-mabda')—indeed the very same entity—so it cannot be possible at one time and impossible at another, since times have no effect on essential possibility. The author notes a possible claim that the first existence confers an increase of preparedness, citing the verse 'and it is easier for Him'. He then raises a consideration: an objection might be that the thing is impossible due to a necessary concomitant, but the response is that either that concomitant renders it impossible or not; if not, the objection fails. Following this, the author gives a methodological note explaining that many theological discussions appear unrelated to creed but are actually useful for defending doctrines. He delays the discussion of i'adat al-ma'dum to this chapter because it is specifically needed for proving the Resurrection as existence after annihilation. He then reports that the majority of theologians (mutakallimun) affirm permissibility, while philosophers (hukama') deny it. The Mu'tazila are divided: the Basran school allows re‑creation of substances based on persistence of essences in non‑existence, but differs on accidents. One group absolutely denies re‑creation of accidents on the ground that the re‑created thing would be re‑created by a meaning, leading to an infinite regress; some Ash'aris hold this. The majority deny re‑creation of non‑persistent accidents (sounds, wills) due to their time‑specificity, and for persistent accidents they distinguish between what is within human power (which cannot be re‑created by anyone) and what is not (which may be re‑created). The author then returns to his own school's proofs: the iqna' argument based on the principle of possibility (quoting the philosophers' maxim), and the ilzam argument that the return is identical to the beginning. He refutes the objection that 'return' (existence a second time) is more specific than absolute existence, so possibility of the general does not entail possibility of the specific. He also discusses a related point: the non‑existent possible is receptive to existence; the first existence may increase preparedness, making the second existence easier. Finally, he interprets the verse 'and it is easier for Him' as referring to the re‑creation of disintegrated parts (not the re‑creation of something from absolute non‑existence), citing another verse about giving life to bones. The passage ends incompletely (cut off at page end).

Key Terms

المعاد
المبدأ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that re‑creating the non‑existent is impossible because it would be a second creation, and a thing cannot be created twice.
Correction: Al‑Taftazani argues that the return is the same entity as the first creation; if the first was possible, the second is equally possible. Times do not affect essential possibility.

Checkpoint
According to the iqna' argument, what is the default judgment for an action before a proof of necessity or impossibility arises?
A) Necessity
B) Impossibility
C) Possibility
D) Indeterminate

Key Takeaway
Re‑creating the non‑existent is permissible because possibility is the default and the return is identical to the first creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that God can re-create you exactly as you are, how does that change the way you approach death? What specific fear or anxiety about dying do you need to surrender today because of this truth?
?
The principle of default possibility (الأصل هو الإمكان) teaches us to withhold judgment until clear evidence. Is there a negative thought you hold about God's justice or mercy that is based on assumption rather than revelation? Will you commit to testing that thought against the Qur'an and Sunnah this week?
?
The ilzam argument says the return is like the beginning. Do you live as if your existence began by mere chance or as a deliberate act of the All-Powerful? How should remembering that your beginning was willed by God change how you seek meaning and purpose today?

Unseen Matters

Usefulness of Theological Discussions and Sectarian Positions
Al-Taftazani explains the usefulness and reports sectarian positions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al‑Taftazani considers discussions like re‑creating the non‑existent essential for defending religious beliefs, and you will learn the positions of theologians, philosophers, and Mu'tazila on this issue.

Core Idea
Seemingly abstract theological debates are crucial for proving resurrection and repelling doubts.

Al‑Taftazani takes a step back to justify why he included this investigation. He explains that many topics that appear unrelated to creed are actually vital for defending doctrines like the Resurrection. Then he surveys the different schools: the majority of theologians affirm re‑creation, the philosophers deny it, and the Mu'tazila have complex internal divisions.

Guided Path
1
Understand the methodological justification
Read the passage where al‑Taftazani explains that many theological investigations (like i'adat al-ma'dum) seem alien to creed but are beneficial for proofs and refuting doubts. Note the examples he gives.
This justifies why this topic is placed in the chapter on al‑ma'ad.
2
Identify the positions of the three groups
List the majority of mutakallimun (theologians) who affirm permissibility, the philosophers (hukama') who deny it, and the Mu'tazila sub-groups.
The Mu'tazila have nuanced views on substances vs. accidents.
3
Focus on the Mu'tazila division on accidents
Some Mu'tazila absolutely deny re‑creation of accidents because it would entail a meaning subsisting in a meaning. Others deny only non‑persistent accidents (sounds, wills) due to time‑specificity. For persistent accidents, they distinguish between those within human power and those beyond.
This shows the diversity within the Mu'tazila school.
