Refuting the Purpose Objection to Resurrection
Al-Taftazani refutes the objection that resurrection without a purpose is absurd.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Taftazani refutes the objection that bodily resurrection must serve a purpose, using the method of 'prevention' (manʿ) to block each premise.

Core Idea
Resurrection's purpose is not pleasure or pain, but just recompense.

In this passage, al-Taftazani addresses a sophisticated objection against bodily resurrection based on the necessity of purpose for a wise agent. The objector argues that any purpose for resurrection would be either for God (deficient) or for servants (impossible). The response uses a series of 'preventions' to dismantle the objection, showing that purpose can be simply giving what is due.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the structure: the objection is presented first, followed by the answer with multiple 'preventions'.
The objection is summarized in the first part, and the answer begins with 'والجواب'.
2
Identify the objection's three parts
The objector argues that resurrection cannot have a purpose: not for God (implies deficiency), not for servants (reduces to pleasure or pain, which are impossible). Identify these parts.
The objection is framed as 'Third: That resurrection...'.
3
Analyze the four preventions
The answer consists of four 'manʿ' (prevention) statements. Note each one: denying necessity of purpose, denying restriction to pleasure/pain, denying that pleasure is mere release from pain, and denying that hereafter pleasures are same as worldly.
Each prevention blocks a premise of the objection.
4
Reflect on the method
Consider how this argument uses logical denial rather than positive proof. It shows that the objector's premises are not necessary, so the objection fails.
This is a common dialectical method in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث - أن الإعادة لا لغرض عبث لا يليق بالحكيم، ولغرض عائد إلى الله تعالى نقص يجب تنزيهه عنه، ولغرض عائد إلى العباد أيضاً باطل، لأنه إما إيصال ألم، وهو لا يليق بالحكيم، وإما إيصال لذة ولا لذة في الوجود، سيما في عالم الحس. فكل ما يتخيل لذة فإنما هو خلاص عن الألم، ولا ألم في العدم أو الموت، ليكون الخلاص عنه لذة مقصودة بالإعادة، بل إنما يتصور ذلك بأن يوصل إليه ألماً ثم يخلصه عنه، فتكون الإعادة لإيصال ألم يعقبه خلاص وهو غير لائق بالحكمة. والجواب - منع اللزوم الغرض، وقبح الخلو عنه في فعل الله تعالى. ثم منع انحصار الغرض في إيصال اللذة والألم، إذ يجوز أن يكون نفس إيصال الجزاء إلى من يستحقه غرضاً، ثم منع كون اللذة دفعاً للألم وخلاصاً عنه. كيف واللذة والألم من الوجدانيات التي لا يشك العاقل في تحققها، وقد سبق تحقيق ذلك، ثم منع كون اللذات الأخروية من جنس الدنيوية بحسب الحقيقة ليلزم كونها دفعاً للألم وخلاصاً عنه.
Third: That resurrection is not without a purpose—absurdity is not befitting the Wise; and for a purpose returning to God is a deficiency from which He must be exalted; and for a purpose returning to the servants is also false, because it is either causing pain, which is not befitting the Wise, or causing pleasure, and there is no pleasure in existence, especially in the sensible world. For everything imagined as pleasure is only a release from pain, and there is no pain in non-existence or death, so that release from it could be a pleasure intended by resurrection. Rather, that is only conceived by causing pain to him and then releasing him from it, so resurrection would be for causing pain followed by release, which is not befitting wisdom. The answer: Prevention of the necessity of purpose and the ugliness of lacking it in God's act. Then prevention of the restriction of purpose to causing pleasure and pain, for it is permissible that the very giving of recompense to the one who deserves it is a purpose. Then prevention that pleasure is a repulsion of pain and a release from it. How? For pleasure and pain are among the intuitive experiences whose reality no rational person doubts, and its investigation has preceded. Then prevention that the pleasures of the Hereafter are of the same kind as worldly pleasures in reality, so that they would necessarily be a repulsion of pain and a release from it.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes an objection against bodily resurrection (al-iʿāda) based on the concept of purpose (al-gharaḍ). The objector argues that resurrection must have a purpose, but it cannot have a purpose: it cannot be for God (as that implies deficiency), nor for the servants, because any purpose for them reduces to causing pleasure or pain. They claim there is no real pleasure in existence, and imagined pleasure is merely release from pain; since there is no pain in non-existence, resurrection cannot aim at release from pain. Thus resurrection would be for causing pain followed by release, which is unbefitting wisdom. The answer (al-jawāb) consists of several 'preventions' (manʿ): First, the necessity of purpose in God's acts is denied. Second, the restriction of purpose to pleasure and pain is denied; giving recompense to the deserving can be a purpose. Third, the claim that pleasure is merely repulsion of pain is denied, as pleasure and pain are distinct intuitive experiences. Fourth, even if that were true, the pleasures of the Hereafter are not of the same nature as worldly pleasures, so the objection collapses. The argument follows a standard kalam format: objection then multiple 'manʿ' responses, each blocking a premise.

Key Terms
الإعادة
الغرض
اللذة
الألم
الحكيم
منع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the objection is about God's need for purpose; actually it's about the absurdity of purposeless action for a wise agent.
Correction: The objection is that a wise being cannot act without a purpose, not that God needs something. The refutation shows purpose is not required or is of a different kind.

Checkpoint
What is the main basis of the objector's argument that resurrection cannot have a purpose?
A) Resurrection must either cause pleasure or pain, but neither is possible.
B) Resurrection is impossible because bodies decay.
C) God cannot perform actions that involve time.
D) The soul does not survive death.

Key Takeaway
Al-Taftazani refutes the purpose-based objection by denying its premises and expanding the concept of divine purpose.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The objector claims all pleasure is merely relief from pain. When you look at your own desire for Paradise, is it driven more by fear of Hell or by a positive longing for the beatific vision? What would change if you truly believed the pleasures of the Hereafter are of an entirely different kind, not just a compensation for worldly suffering?
?
Al-Taftazani argues that God does not need a purpose to act wisely. Do you sometimes find yourself questioning God's wisdom in your trials because you cannot see a purpose? How can this lesson's reminder that God's wisdom is not bound by human purposes reshape your response to unexplained hardships?
?
The objector assumes that resurrection must either give pleasure or pain, but al-Taftazani asserts that the very act of giving recompense is a purpose in itself. How does that shift your understanding of the Day of Judgment—from a transaction of rewards and punishments to a profound display of divine justice? In what way does that make you more conscious of your deeds even when no immediate consequence is visible?

Understanding Spiritual Resurrection: Definition and Possibilities
Al-Taftazani defines spiritual resurrection and states it needs no further proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two interpretations of spiritual resurrection presented by al-Taftazani and why he considers it automatically proven once the soul's survival is established.

Core Idea
Spiritual resurrection is the soul's return to its original state or its reattachment to the body.

Al-Taftazani begins this note by asserting that proving the soul's abstraction and survival after death automatically proves spiritual resurrection. He then defines spiritual resurrection in two ways: either the soul returns to pure abstraction, free from bodily attachments, or it becomes attached to the resurrected body. This lesson explores these definitions and the initial claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic source passage once through, then the translation. Focus on the first part where the claim and definitions are given.
2
Identify the two definitions
Find where al-Taftazani says 'it is either... or...'. Note the two possibilities: return to pure abstraction or attachment to the resurrected body.
The second possibility is immediately criticized as not intelligible or transmitted.
3
Understand the claim of no further proof
Why does al-Taftazani say that after proving the soul's survival, spiritual resurrection needs no extra proof? Because it is simply the soul's return to its original state or reattachment.
The proof of the soul's survival already establishes that the soul can exist without the body.
4
Consider the problem with the second definition
Note the author's remark that attachment to the resurrected body is 'neither intelligible nor transmitted'. What does this imply about which definition is intended?
This suggests the primary meaning is the return to pure abstraction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال: تنبيه بعد إثبات تجرد النفس وبقائها بعد خراب البدن لا يفتقر إثبات المعاد الروحاني إلى زيادة بيان، لأنه عبارة إما عن عودها إلى ما كانت عليه من التجرد المحض، أو التبرؤ من ظلمات التعلق ملتذة أو متألمة بما اكتسبت، وإما عن تعلقها بالبدن المحشور الذي ليس بمعقول ولا منقول، إما أن تتعلق به نفس أخرى، وتبقى نفسها معطلة أو متعلقة ببدن آخر. القائلون بالمعاد الروحاني فقط، أو به وبالجسماني جميعاً هم الذين يقولون بأن النفوس الناطقة مجردة باقية لا تفنى بخراب البدن لما سيق من الدلائل، ويشهد بذلك نصوص من الكتاب والسنة، فلا حاجة للأولين إلى زيادة بيان في إثبات المعاد، لأنه عبارة عن عود النفس إلى ما كانت عليه من التجرد أو التبرؤ من ظلمات التعلق وبقائها ملتذة بالكمال أو متألمة بالنقصان، ولا للآخرين بعد إثبات حشر الأجساد، لأن القول بإحياء البدن مع تعلق نفس أخرى به تدبر أمره وبقاء نفسه معطلة، أو متعلقة ببدن آخر غير مقبول عند العقل، ولا منقول من ونفسها مناسبة لذلك المزاج، آلفة به لم تفارقه إلا لانتفاء قابليته لتصرفاتها. فحين عادت القابلية، عاد التعلق لا محالة. وقد يقال إن قوله تعالى: {فلا تعلم نفس ما أخفي لهم من قرة أعين} للذين أحسنوا الحسنى وزيادة ورضوان من الله أكبر إشارة إلى المعاد الروحاني، وكذا الأحاديث الواردة في حال أرواح المؤمنين.
He said: A note. After the proof of the soul's abstraction and its survival after the body's decay, the proof of spiritual resurrection does not require additional explanation, because it is either (the soul's) return to what it was of pure abstraction, or dissociation from the darknesses of attachment, experiencing pleasure or pain due to what it acquired; or (it consists of) its attachment to the resurrected body—which is neither intelligible nor transmitted—either that another soul attaches to it, and its own soul remains idle or attached to another body. Those who affirm only spiritual resurrection, or both spiritual and bodily resurrection, are those who say that the rational souls are abstract, surviving, not perishing with the body's decay due to the evidences presented, and texts from the Book and the Sunnah testify to that. So the former have no need for additional explanation in proving resurrection, because it is the soul's return to what it was of abstraction or dissociation from the darknesses of attachment, and its remaining experiencing pleasure by perfection or pain by deficiency. Nor do the latter (need additional explanation) after the proof of the gathering of bodies, because the assertion that the body is revived with another soul attached to it managing its affairs while its own soul remains idle or attached to another body is unacceptable to reason, nor is it transmitted—and its own soul is suitable for that temperament, familiar with it, not separating from it except due to the loss of its capacity for its actions. So when the capacity returns, attachment returns necessarily. It may be said that His statement, the Exalted, {No soul knows what has been hidden for them of comfort for the eyes} for those who do good, the best and more, and the pleasure of God is greater, is an indication of spiritual resurrection, and likewise the hadiths concerning the state of the souls of the believers.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a note (tanbīh) by the author on spiritual resurrection (al-maʿād al-rūḥānī). It begins by stating that once the soul's abstraction and survival after bodily decay are proven, proving spiritual resurrection needs no further explanation. The author then defines spiritual resurrection in two ways: either the soul returns to its original state of pure abstraction, or it dissociates from attachments while experiencing pleasure or pain from its acquisitions. Another possibility is attachment to the resurrected body, but that is not rationally or textually established. Those who accept only spiritual resurrection, or both spiritual and bodily, hold that rational souls are abstract and survive bodily decay, based on proofs from reason and revelation. The first group needs no further proof for spiritual resurrection. The second group, after proving bodily resurrection, need no further proof because the soul naturally reattaches to its familiar body when the body regains receptivity. The author quotes a Quranic verse (Sajdah 32:17) and mentions hadiths about the souls of believers as evidence for spiritual resurrection.

Key Terms
المعاد الروحاني
تجرد النفس
التعلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Spiritual resurrection means a completely new spiritual existence created independently.
Correction: Spiritual resurrection is the same soul returning to its original state of abstraction, not a new creation.

Checkpoint
According to al-Taftazani, what is the primary definition of spiritual resurrection?
A) The soul's attachment to a new resurrected body.
B) The soul's return to pure abstraction after dissociation from the body.
C) The soul's reincarnation in another body.
D) The soul's annihilation and recreation.

Key Takeaway
Spiritual resurrection is the soul's return to its original dissociation from bodily attachments, automatically proven once the soul's survival is established.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your soul were to be stripped of all bodily attachments right now, what would it experience—pleasure or pain? How do your daily choices today shape that answer?
?
You claim to believe that the soul survives death and returns to its original state. Does your lifestyle reflect that you are truly convinced, or do you live as if this world is all there is?
?
The passage says spiritual resurrection needs no further proof once the soul's abstraction is established. Does your certainty about the afterlife match that logical conclusion, or do you still harbor doubts that affect your actions? How will you address those doubts starting today?

Why Bodily Resurrection Implies Spiritual Resurrection
Al-Taftazani argues that bodily resurrection entails spiritual resurrection due to the soul's natural reattachment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Taftazani's argument that those who affirm bodily resurrection do not need additional proof for spiritual resurrection because the soul naturally reattaches to its body.

Core Idea
The soul's natural attachment to its body ensures that bodily resurrection includes spiritual resurrection.

After presenting the definitions, al-Taftazani addresses two groups: those who affirm only spiritual resurrection and those who affirm both. He argues that for the latter, once bodily resurrection is proven, spiritual resurrection is automatically implied because the soul is suited to its body and reattaches when the body regains receptivity. This lesson examines that reasoning and its support from revelation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two groups
The author mentions 'those who affirm only spiritual resurrection' and 'those who affirm both spiritual and bodily resurrection'. Both groups hold that the soul is abstract and survives.
They are distinguished by whether they accept bodily resurrection in addition.
2
Understand the argument for the second group
For those who affirm bodily resurrection, once bodily resurrection is proven, spiritual resurrection follows automatically. Why? Because the soul is naturally attached to its body and only left due to the body's loss of capacity. When the body is resurrected and regains capacity, the soul reattaches necessarily.
This argument relies on the soul's suitability (munāsaba) for its particular body.
3
Reject alternative possibilities
Al-Taftazani rejects the idea that another soul could attach to the body while the original soul remains idle or attaches elsewhere. This is unacceptable to reason and not supported by revelation.
The soul and body have a unique affinity; replacement is impossible.
4
Examine the scriptural evidence
The author quotes Quran 32:17 about the hidden comfort for the righteous and mentions hadiths about the state of believers' souls, indicating spiritual resurrection.
These texts are seen as indications (ishāra) of spiritual resurrection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

He said: A note. After the proof of the soul's abstraction and its survival after the body's decay, the proof of spiritual resurrection does not require additional explanation, because it is either (the soul's) return to what it was of pure abstraction, or dissociation from the darknesses of attachment, experiencing pleasure or pain due to what it acquired; or (it consists of) its attachment to the resurrected body—which is neither intelligible nor transmitted—either that another soul attaches to it, and its own soul remains idle or attached to another body. Those who affirm only spiritual resurrection, or both spiritual and bodily resurrection, are those who say that the rational souls are abstract, surviving, not perishing with the body's decay due to the evidences presented, and texts from the Book and the Sunnah testify to that. So the former have no need for additional explanation in proving resurrection, because it is the soul's return to what it was of abstraction or dissociation from the darknesses of attachment, and its remaining experiencing pleasure by perfection or pain by deficiency. Nor do the latter (need additional explanation) after the proof of the gathering of bodies, because the assertion that the body is revived with another soul attached to it managing its affairs while its own soul remains idle or attached to another body is unacceptable to reason, nor is it transmitted—and its own soul is suitable for that temperament, familiar with it, not separating from it except due to the loss of its capacity for its actions. So when the capacity returns, attachment returns necessarily. It may be said that His statement, the Exalted, {No soul knows what has been hidden for them of comfort for the eyes} for those who do good, the best and more, and the pleasure of God is greater, is an indication of spiritual resurrection, and likewise the hadiths concerning the state of the souls of the believers.

This passage is a note (tanbīh) by the author on spiritual resurrection (al-maʿād al-rūḥānī). It begins by stating that once the soul's abstraction and survival after bodily decay are proven, proving spiritual resurrection needs no further explanation. Key Terms

الحشور
التعلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Bodily resurrection and spiritual resurrection are two separate, independent events.
Correction: Al-Taftazani shows that bodily resurrection automatically includes spiritual resurrection because the same soul returns to its body.

Checkpoint
According to al-Taftazani, why does bodily resurrection automatically imply spiritual resurrection?
A) Because the soul is created at the same time as the body.
B) Because the soul naturally reattaches to its body when the body regains receptivity.
C) Because spiritual resurrection is irrelevant to bodily resurrection.
D) Because the soul is annihilated and recreated with the body.

Key Takeaway
Bodily resurrection entails spiritual resurrection because the soul naturally returns to its body when it becomes receptive.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You believe in the resurrection of the body, but do you truly believe that the same soul that sins and repents today will be held accountable before Allah on that Day? If so, how does this certainty change the way you treat your body and soul right now?
?
If the soul's attachment to the body is based on suitability and familiarity, then your soul has been shaped by your deeds in this world. What specific, persistent habits of thought or action are making your soul less suitable for Paradise? What will you change today?

Refuting the Equating of Pleasures and Defining Spiritual Resurrection
Refutation of equating pleasures and definition of spiritual resurrection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's refutation of equating worldly and otherworldly pleasures, and the two ways spiritual resurrection is defined after the soul's survival.

Core Idea
Spiritual resurrection is either the soul's return to incorporeality or its attachment to a resurrected body.

The author begins by rejecting the claim that otherworldly pleasures are of the same genus as worldly ones, which would reduce them to mere pain removal. He then introduces a crucial note: once the soul's incorporeality and survival are proven, spiritual resurrection requires no further proof. This lesson unpacks that note and the two definitions of spiritual resurrection.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation of equating pleasures
Read the first sentence carefully. Notice how the author preemptively blocks a potential objection that would reduce otherworldly pleasures to mere relief from pain.
This refutation is a 'manع' (prevention) in kalam style.
2
Understand the note on spiritual resurrection
After the refutation, the author states that proving the soul's survival makes spiritual resurrection self-evident. Identify the two definitions he gives: (1) return to pure incorporeality, (2) attachment to a resurrected body.
He uses 'imma... aw' (either... or) structure.
3
Distinguish the two groups of believers
The author mentions those who affirm only spiritual resurrection and those who affirm both. Note that both groups agree on the soul's incorporeality and survival. The difference lies in whether they also accept bodily resurrection.
The first group needs no extra proof for spiritual resurrection; the second group already has proof for bodily gathering.
4
Analyze the argument about soul-body attachment
Read the passage where the author argues that a soul suited to a body does not leave it except due to loss of capacity. When capacity returns, attachment is inevitable. This supports the bodily resurrection view.
This argument relies on 'munasabah' (suitability) between soul and body.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم منع كون اللذات الأخروية من جنس الدنيوية بحسب الحقيقة ليلزم كونها دفعاً للألم وخلاصاً عنه . قال : تنبيه) (تنبيه) بعد إثبات تجرد النفس وبقائها بعد خراب البدن لا يفتقر إثبات المعاد الروحاني إلى زيادة بيان، لأنه عبارة إما عن عودها إلى ما كانت عليه من التجرد المحض (۳) ، أو التبرؤ من ظلمات التعلق ملتذة أو متألمة، بما اكتسبت (۳) وإما عن تعلقها بالبدن المحشور الذي ليس بمعقول ولا منقول، إما أن تتعلق به نفس أخرى، وتبقى نفسها معطلة أو متعلقة ببدن آخر . القائلون بالمعاد الروحاني فقط، أو به، وبالجسماني جميعاً هم الذين يقولون بأن النفوس الناطقة مجردة باقية لا تفنى بخراب البدن لما سيق من الدلائل، ويشهد بذلك نصوص من الكتاب والسنة، فلا حاجة للأولين إلى زيادة بيان في إثبات المعاد، لأنه عبارة عن عود النفس إلى ما كانت عليه من التجرد أو التبرؤ من ظلمات التعلق وبقائها ملتذة بالكمال أو متألمة بالنقصان ولا للآخرين بعد إثبات حشر الأجساد، لأن القول بإحياء البدن مع تعلق نفس أخرى به تدبر أمره وبقاء نفسه معطلة، أو متعلقة ببدن آخر غير مقبول عند العقل، ولا منقول من ونفسها مناسبة لذلك المزاج، آلفة به لم تفارقه إلا لانتفاء قابليته لتصرفاتها. فحين عادت القابلية، عاد التعلق لا محالة. وقد يقال إن قوله تعالى : {فلا تعلم نفس ما أخفي لهم من قرة أعين} (٤) للذين أحسنوا الحسنى وزيادة (٥) ورضوان من الله أكبر (٦) إشارة إلى المعاد الروحاني، وكذا الأحاديث الواردة في حال أرواح المؤمنين، وخصوصاً الصديقين والشهداء والصالحين، وأنها في حواصل طيور خضر في قناديل من نور معلقة تحت العرش، وإن كانت ظواهرها مشعرة بأن الأرواح من قبيل الأجسام على ما قال إمام الحرمين أن الأظهر عندنا أن الأرواح أجسام لطيفة مشابكة للأجسام المحسوسة، أجرى الله تعالى العادة باستمرار حياة الأجساد ما استمرت مشابكتها بها فإذا فارقها، يعقب الموت الحياة في استمرار العادة، ثم الروح يعرج به ، ويرفع في حواصل طيور خضر في الجنة، ويهبط به إلى سجين من الكفرة كما وردت فيه الآثار والحياة عرض يحيى به الجوهر . والروح يحيا بالحياة أيضاً إن قامت به الحياة، فهذا قولنا في الروح، كذا في الإرشاد.
Then he prevented that the otherworldly pleasures are of the same genus as worldly ones according to reality so that they would be repelling pain and deliverance from it. He said: A note. (Note) After establishing the soul's incorporeality and its survival after the body's destruction, the proof of spiritual resurrection does not need further elaboration, because it is either a return to what it was of pure incorporeality, or dissociation from the darkness of attachment, experiencing pleasure or pain, according to what it acquired, or its attachment to the resurrected body which is neither rational nor transmitted, either that another soul attaches to it and its own soul remains idle or attached to another body. Those who affirm only spiritual resurrection, or both it and bodily resurrection, are those who say that rational souls are incorporeal, surviving, not perishing with the body's destruction, due to the proofs that have been presented, and texts from the Book and Sunnah testify to that. So the first group needs no further explanation in proving resurrection, because it is the soul's return to what it was of incorporeality or dissociation from the darkness of attachment and its remaining enjoying perfection or suffering deficiency. And the second group after proving the gathering of bodies, because the statement of reviving the body while another soul attaches to it to manage its affair and its own soul remains idle, or attached to another body, is not acceptable to reason, nor transmitted from... And its soul is suitable for that temperament, familiar with it, not leaving it except due to the loss of its capacity for its actions. So when capacity returns, attachment returns inevitably. And it may be said that His statement, exalted: 'No soul knows what joy is kept hidden for them' ... is an indication of spiritual resurrection, and likewise the hadiths reported about the state of the souls of believers, especially the truthful, martyrs, and righteous, that they are in the crops of green birds in lanterns of light hung under the Throne, even if their apparent meanings suggest that souls are of the type of bodies, according to what Imam al-Haramayn said: the apparent view with us is that souls are subtle bodies intertwined with sensible bodies, God, exalted, has made the habit continue of the life of bodies as long as their intertwining with them continues. So when it leaves them, death follows life in the continuation of habit. Then the soul ascends, is raised in the crops of green birds in Paradise, and is brought down to Sijjin of the disbelievers as reported in the traditions. And life is an accident that gives life to the substance. And the soul also lives by life if life subsists in it. This is our saying about the soul, as in al-Irshad.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage begins with a refutation of the claim that otherworldly pleasures are of the same genus as worldly ones, which would imply they are merely the removal of pain. Then the author introduces a note (تنبيه) on spiritual resurrection. He states that after proving the soul's incorporeality and survival after the body's destruction, proving spiritual resurrection requires no further explanation. He defines spiritual resurrection in two ways: either the soul returns to its original disembodied state, free from attachment, experiencing pleasure or pain based on its deeds; or it attaches to a resurrected body that is neither knowable by reason nor reported. The author then distinguishes between two groups: those who affirm only spiritual resurrection (and need no extra proof) and those who affirm both spiritual and bodily resurrection. For the latter, after proving bodily resurrection, the soul's attachment to its original body is necessary if the soul is suited to that body. He cites Quranic verse 32:17 as evidence for spiritual resurrection, and mentions hadiths about the souls of believers being in the crops of green birds in lanterns under the Throne. He notes that these texts in their apparent meaning suggest that souls are bodies, and reports Imam al-Haramayn's view that souls are subtle bodies intertwined with sensible bodies, such that life continues as long as the intertwining lasts. The passage concludes with a summary: life is an accident that gives life to the substance, and the soul lives by life. This is the view expressed in al-Irshad.

Key Terms
المعاد الروحاني
التجرد
المعاد الجسماني
النفس الناطقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think spiritual resurrection requires a separate body or is just a metaphor.
Correction: The author clarifies it is the soul's return to its incorporeal state or attachment to its original body based on suitability.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does spiritual resurrection not need further proof after establishing the soul's survival?
A) Because the soul is eternal
B) Because it is defined as return to incorporeality or attachment to a body
C) Because it is a matter of faith only
D) Because the author does not provide proof

Key Takeaway
Spiritual resurrection is the soul's return to serenity or rightful attachment, not a separate creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You know that your soul is suited to this specific body and will return to it when capacity returns. If that is true, then your every action now shapes that reunion. Are you living today as if your soul is on a journey back to its Lord, or as if this world is permanent? What one habit will you change this week to align with that reality?
?
The passage says otherworldly pleasures are not like worldly ones—they are not merely the removal of pain. When you imagine Paradise, do you picture it as an escape from discomfort or as a positive attainment of perfection? How does that shift in understanding change your longing for the Hereafter right now?
?
Spiritual resurrection is either a return to pure incorporeality or attachment to a body. Your soul will not be idle. Do you really believe that your deepest happiness is not in accumulating worldly things but in the soul's state of purity or rightful attachment? If so, what are you clinging to today that you must let go of for the sake of that eternal state?

Scriptural Evidence and the Nature of Souls
Scriptural evidence for spiritual resurrection and discussion of the nature of souls

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Quranic and hadith evidence for spiritual resurrection and the author's discussion of whether souls are subtle bodies.

Core Idea
Apparent scriptural evidence suggests souls are subtle bodies, but the essence of resurrection is spiritual.

The author cites Quranic verse 32:17 and several hadiths about the souls of believers in green birds' crops under the Throne. He addresses the implication that these texts seem to depict souls as bodies, and reports Imam al-Haramayn's view that souls are subtle bodies intertwined with physical bodies. This lesson examines that evidence and the author's concluding remarks on life and the soul.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verse and its interpretation
The author quotes verse 32:17 as an indication of spiritual resurrection. Notice how he interprets 'no soul knows what joy is kept hidden' as referring to spiritual delights beyond physical description.
The verse is often cited in discussions of spiritual reward.
2
Examine the hadith evidence
Read the description of believers' souls in green birds' crops in lanterns under the Throne. Understand that these texts, in their apparent meaning, suggest souls are bodies.
Imam al-Haramayn is quoted to clarify this apparent meaning.
3
Analyze Imam al-Haramayn's view on souls
He states that the apparent view is that souls are subtle bodies (ajsam latifa) intertwined with sensible bodies. Life continues as long as this intertwining lasts.
This view attempts to reconcile scriptural language with philosophical concepts.
4
Understand the author's conclusion
The passage concludes by stating that life is an accident that gives life to the substance, and the soul lives by life. This is the position of the Ash'ari school as found in al-Irshad.
The soul is not itself an accident but a substance that receives life.

?

Three Schools on the Annihilation of the Body
Listing three positions on body annihilation with proponents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three distinct opinions among Islamic theologians on how the annihilation of bodies occurs.

Core Idea
Annihilation of bodies is debated among three causes: direct removal, opposite, or missing condition.

After establishing that bodies can be annihilated, theologians differed on the mechanism. Some said God directly annihilates, others said He creates an opposite that destroys, and others said a necessary condition is removed. This passage outlines those positions and their key proponents.

Guided Path
1
Read the classification
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the three main schools. Notice the labels: الأول, الثاني, الثالث.
The passage is a list; look for the structure.
2
Identify sub-opinions
Within each school, note the different theologians and their specific views. For example, Abu al-Hudhayl vs. al-Qadi in the first school.
3
Reflect on incompleteness
The third school is cut off mid-sentence. Consider how the list might continue based on the pattern of the first two schools.
The source text ends with 'وقال أكثر' (and most said...).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث الثالث اختلف القائلون بصحة فناء الجسم في أنه بإعدام معدم، أو بحدوث ضد، أو بانتفاء شرط. أما الأول - فقال القاضي وبعض المعتزلة هو بإعدام الله تعالى بلا واسطة. وقال أبو الهذيل (۱) : بأمر إفن، كالوجود بأمر كن . وأما الثاني - فقال ابن الأخشيد (۳) : يخلق الله تعالى الفناء في جهة معينة، فتفنى الجواهر بأسرها. وقال ابن شبيب (۳) : يخلق الله في كل جوهر فناء، فيقتضي فناءه الزمان الثاني. وقال أبو علي : يخلق بعدد كل جوهر فناء، لا في محل . وقال أبو هاشم (٤) : بل فناء واحداً . وأما الثالث ـ فقال بشر (ه): ذلك الشرط بقاء يخلقه الله، لا في محل . وقال أكثر
The third investigation: Those who affirm the correctness of the annihilation of the body differed whether it is by the non-existence of an annihilator, or by the occurrence of an opposite, or by the absence of a condition. As for the first: al-Qadi and some of the Mu'tazila said it is by God's non-existence without intermediary. And Abu al-Hudhayl said: by a command 'Be annihilated', like existence by a command 'Be'. As for the second: Ibn al-Akhshid said: God creates annihilation in a specific direction, so all atoms perish. And Ibn Shabib said: God creates annihilation in every atom, so its annihilation necessitates the second time. And Abu Ali said: He creates as many annihilations as atoms, not in a locus. And Abu Hashim said: rather one annihilation. As for the third: Bishr said: that condition is a survival that God creates, not in a locus. And most said...
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the different opinions among those who affirm the annihilation of the body (فناء الجسم) regarding its cause. The author divides the debate into three main schools. The first school holds that annihilation occurs by direct removal (إعدام) by God, either without an intermediary (al-Qadi and some Mu'tazila) or by a direct command 'Be annihilated' (Abu al-Hudhayl, comparing to creation by 'Be'). The second school holds that annihilation occurs by the creation of an opposite (ضد). Sub-opinions include: Ibn al-Akhshid says God creates annihilation in a specific direction causing all atoms to perish; Ibn Shabib says God creates annihilation in each atom, causing its perishing in the second moment; Abu Ali says He creates as many annihilations as atoms, not in a locus; Abu Hashim says only one annihilation suffices. The third school holds that annihilation occurs by the removal of a condition (انتفاء شرط). Bishr states that the condition is a survival (بقاء) created by God not in a locus. The passage ends mid-sentence with 'وقال أكثر' (and most said...), indicating the enumeration continues beyond the window.

Key Terms
فناء الجسم
إعدام
حدوث ضد
انتفاء شرط
بقاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that all theologians agreed on a single cause for annihilation.
Correction: The passage shows at least three distinct schools with multiple sub-opinions, indicating significant disagreement.

Checkpoint
According to the text, which school holds that annihilation occurs by the absence of a condition?
A) The first school
B) The second school
C) The third school
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
The cause of body annihilation is a disputed topic among theologians, with three main explanatory frameworks: direct annihilation, creation of an opposite, or removal of a condition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a complex theological debate like this, do you tend to simplify it by favoring one side, or do you patiently examine each position as the scholars did? Reflect on a recent situation where you dismissed a view too quickly. What will you do differently next time?
?
The scholars here differ on how God brings about annihilation—directly, through an opposite, or by removing a condition. Does your understanding of God's absolute power include the ability to annihilate in all these ways? How does this expand your awe of His control over every atom?
?
These theologians devoted their lives to precise thinking about God's actions. Is there an area in your life where you are content with vague or inherited beliefs? What is one specific assumption you hold about God that you have never examined with this level of care, and what step will you take to investigate it?

The Soul: Subtle Body and Afterlife Abode
Sanusi discusses the soul's nature as a subtle body and its abode after death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the classical Ash'ari view that the soul is a subtle body, and what happens to believers' and disbelievers' souls after death.

Core Idea
The soul is a subtle body that continues after death in a sensory abode.

Sanusi presents two interconnected teachings: where the souls of the righteous and wicked go after death, and what the soul actually is. The outward wording suggests souls are bodies, and he defends this by citing Imam al-Haramayn’s view that souls are subtle bodies intertwined with physical ones. This lesson unpacks both the doctrinal content and the rational framework behind it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping, then read the English translation. Notice that the passage moves from describing the afterlife states of souls to defining what the soul is.
The passage includes a citation to Imam al-Haramayn and references al-Irshad.
2
Identify the two abodes
The passage states that righteous souls are in 'crops of green birds in lanterns of light under the Throne' and later ascend to Paradise, while disbelievers' souls are lowered to Sijjin. Identify these two distinct fates.
The phrase 'حواصل طيور خضر' is a well-known hadith description.
3
Understand the soul's nature
The passage defines the soul as a subtle body (jism latif) and life (hayat) as an accident that subsists in it. Notice how this definition is used to explain the soul's separation from the body at death.
This reflects the Ash'ari position that the soul is not purely spiritual but has a bodily aspect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخصوصاً الصديقين والشهداء والصالحين، وأنها في حواصل طيور خضر في قناديل من نور معلقة تحت العرش، وإن كانت ظواهرها مشعرة بأن الأرواح من قبيل الأجسام على ما قال إمام الحرمين أن الأظهر عندنا أن الأرواح أجسام لطيفة مشابكة للأجسام المحسوسة، أجرى الله تعالى العادة باستمرار حياة الأجساد ما استمرت مشابكتها بها فإذا فارقها، يعقب الموت الحياة في إستمرار العادة، ثم · الروح يعرج به ، ويرفع في حواصل طيور خضر في الجنة، ويهبط به إلى سجين من الكفرة كما وردت فيه الآثار والحياة عرض يحيى به الجوهر . والروح يحيا بالحياة ايضاً إن قامت به الحياة، فهذا قولنا في الروح، كذا في الإرشاد.
And especially the truthful, the martyrs, and the righteous, and that they are in the crops of green birds in lanterns of light suspended beneath the Throne, even though their apparent meanings indicate that souls are of the category of bodies, according to what Imam al-Haramayn said: that the apparent to us is that souls are subtle bodies intertwined with sensible bodies. Allah, may He be exalted, has customary practice of continuing the life of bodies as long as their intertwining with them continues. When it separates from them, death follows life in the continuity of habit. Then the soul ascends with him, and is raised in the crops of green birds in Paradise, and is lowered to Sijjin (a place in Hell) for the disbelievers, as reported in the traditions. Life is an accident by which the substance is animated. And the soul also lives by life if life subsists in it. This is our saying concerning the soul. Thus in al-Irshad.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage defines the soul (ruh) and its state after death. It begins by stating that the souls of the truthful, martyrs, and righteous are placed in the crops of green birds in lanterns of light under the Throne. Then it addresses a potential objection: the outward meaning suggests souls are bodies. It quotes Imam al-Haramayn, who asserts that the apparent view is that souls are subtle bodies (ajsam latifa) intertwined with physical bodies. Allah's custom is that bodies remain alive as long as the soul stays intertwined; when it separates, death follows. The passage then describes the soul's fate: the believer's soul ascends and resides in green birds in Paradise, while the disbeliever's soul is lowered to Sijjin. It defines life (hayat) as an accident that animates the substance, and confirms that the soul lives by that life if life subsists in it. The passage concludes by attributing this position to al-Irshad.

Key Terms
روح
أجسام لطيفة
حياة
عرض
حواصل
سجين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The soul is a purely non-physical spirit with no bodily aspects.
Correction: Classical Sunni kalam, as represented by Sanusi and Imam al-Haramayn, holds that the soul is a subtle body, not a purely spiritual entity.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what happens to the soul of a disbeliever after death?
A) It is placed in green birds in Paradise.
B) It is lowered to Sijjin.
C) It remains with the body.
D) It ascends to the Throne.

Key Takeaway
The soul is a subtle body whose post-mortem destination—whether green birds in Paradise or Sijjin—reflects its nature and the person's faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your soul is a subtle body that will soon separate from your physical body. Where is it headed—to the lanterns under the Throne or to Sijjin? What in your life today points to that destination?
?
The soul lives by life if life subsists in it. Is your soul alive with obedience and faith, or are you merely existing? What habit will you change to ensure your soul is truly alive?
?
The truthful and martyrs are in green birds—are you striving to be among them? What sacrifice have you made today that proves your sincerity?

Preliminary Views on Permanence and the Threefold Division of Annihilation
Lists four views on permanence and introduces three categories of annihilation causes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different theological positions on the nature of permanence (baqa') in bodies and recognize three general categories explaining how bodies undergo annihilation (fana').

Core Idea
Permanence is not a thing but a descriptive attribute, while annihilation has three possible causes.

Sanusi begins by reporting how various scholars define the permanence of bodies: some as a created accident, others as the accidents themselves, others as states (akwan), and al-Nazzam as continuous creation. He then reaffirms that bodies are permanent yet annihilable, and introduces the fundamental division of annihilation into three possible mechanisms: by direct removal, by opposite, or by removal of a condition. This sets the stage for the detailed arguments that follow.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the opening segment carefully to understand the different positions on permanence.
Note the key term 'baqa'' and its variants.
2
Identify the four positions on baqa'
List each scholar or group and their definition of permanence.
Al-Qadi has two opinions, but here he gives one.
3
Understand the status of bodies
The passage states bodies are permanent but not eternal, contrary to philosophers and some others.
This is a theological stance.
4
Observe the threefold classification
Notice the sentence introducing three theories: by removal of a remover, by occurrence of an opposite, or by removal of a condition.
This classification structures the entire debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أصحابنا بقاء قائم بالجسم يخلق الله فيه حالاً فحالاً. وقال إمام الحرمين الأعراض التي تحت اتصاف الجسم بها. وقال القاضي في أحد قوليه : الأكوان التي يخلقها فيه حالاً فحالاً . وقال النظام : خلقه لأنه ليس بباق، بل يخلق حالاً فحالاً . قد سبقت في مباحث الجسم إشارة إلى أن الأجسام باقية، غير متزايلة على ما يراه النظام، وقابلة للفناء، غير دائمة للبقاء على ما يراه الفلاسفة قولاً بأنها أزلية أبدية . والجاحظ ، وجمع من الكرامية قولاً بأنها أبدية، غير أزلية. وتوقف أصحاب أبي الحسين في صحة الفناء واختلف القائلون بها في أن الفناء بإعدام معدم، أو بحدوث ضد، أو بانتفاء شرط. أما الأول - فذهب القاضي، وبعض المعتزلة إلى أن الله تعالى يعدم العالم بلا واسطة، فيصير معدوماً كما أوجده كذلك ، فصار موجوداً. وذهب أبو الهذيل إلى أنه تعالى يقول له : «افنَ، فيفنى كما قال له : كن فكان . وأما الثاني - فذهب جمهور المعتزلة إلى أن فناء الجوهر بحدوث ضد له الفناء، ثم اختلفوا فذهب ابن الأخشيد إلى أن الفناء، وإن لم يكن متحيزاً، لكنه يكون حاصلاً في جهة معينة . فإذا أحدثه الله تعالى فيها، عدمت الجواهر بأسرها. وذهب ابن شبيب إلى أن الله تعالى يحدث في كل جوهر فناء، ثم ذلك الفناء يقتضي عدم الجوهر في الزمان الثاني . وذهب أبو علي وأتباعه إلى أنه يخلق بعدد كل جوهر فناء لا في محل، فتفنى الجواهر. وقال أبو هاشم وأشياعه يخلق فناء واحد لا في محل، فتفنى به الجواهر بأسرها. وأما الثالث - وهو أن فناء الجوهر بانقطاع شرط وجوده . فزعم بشر أن ذلك الشرط بقاء يخلقه الله تعالى لا في محل، فإذا لم يوجد عدم الجوهر. وذهب الأكثرون من أصحابنا والكعبي من المعتزلة إلى أنه بقاء قائم به، يخلقه الله تعالى حالاً فحالاً. فإذا لم يخلقه الله تعالى فيه، انتفى الجوهر . وقال إمام الحرمين بأنها الأعراض التي يجب اتصاف الجسم بها. فإذا يخلقها الله فيه فني . وقال القاضي في أحد قوليه : هو الأكوان التي يخلقها الله تعالى في الجسم حالاً فحالاً. فمتى لم يخلقها فيه انعدم . وقال النظام إنه ليس بباق، بل يخلق حالاً فحالاً فمتى لم يخلق فني . وأكثر هذه الأقاويل من قبيل الأباطيل ، سيما القول: يكون الفناء أمراً محققاً في الخارج، وضداً للبقاء، قائماً بنفسه، أو بالجوهر، وكون البقاء موجوداً إلا في محل، ولعل وجه البطلان غني عن البيان .
Our companions [hold that] permanence (baqa') is an accident subsisting in the body, which God creates in it moment by moment. And Imam al-Haramayn [said]: the accidents (a'rad) by which the body is characterized. And al-Qadi in one of his two opinions [said]: the states (akwan) which He creates in it moment by moment. And al-Nazzam said: His creation [of it] because it is not permanent, rather He creates it moment by moment. There has already preceded, in the investigations of the body, an indication that bodies are permanent, not disintegrating according to al-Nazzam's view, and susceptible to annihilation, not eternal in permanence according to the philosophers' view, saying that they are eternal and everlasting. And al-Jahiz, and a group of the Karramiyya, saying that they are everlasting, not eternal. And the followers of Abu al-Husayn suspended judgment on the validity of annihilation. And those who affirmed it differed concerning whether annihilation is by the removal of a remover, or by the occurrence of an opposite, or by the removal of a condition. As for the first [view]: al-Qadi and some of the Mu'tazila went that God Most High annihilates the world without intermediary, so it becomes non-existent just as He brought it into existence in that manner, so it became existent. And Abu al-Hudhayl went that He Most High says to it: 'Perish!', so it perishes just as He said to it: 'Be!', so it was. As for the second [view]: the majority of the Mu'tazila went that the annihilation of the substance (jawhar) is by the occurrence of an opposite (didd) to it, namely annihilation. Then they differed: Ibn al-Akhshid went that annihilation, although not extended (mutahayyiz), occurs in a specific direction. So when God Most High produces it therein, all the substances become annihilated. And Ibn Shabib went that God Most High creates in every substance an annihilation, then that annihilation necessitates the non-existence of the substance in the second moment. And Abu 'Ali and his followers went that He creates for every substance an annihilation not in a locus (la fi mahall), so the substances become annihilated. And Abu Hashim and his followers said: He creates a single annihilation not in a locus, so by it all the substances become annihilated. As for the third [view]: that the annihilation of the substance is by the cessation of a condition of its existence. Bishr claimed that that condition is a permanence (baqa') which God Most High creates not in a locus, so if it does not exist, the substance becomes non-existent. And the majority of our companions and al-Ka'bi of the Mu'tazila went that it is a permanence subsisting in it, which God Most High creates in it moment by moment. So if God Most High does not create it in it, the substance ceases. And Imam al-Haramayn said that they are the accidents by which the body must be characterized. So if he creates them in it, it perishes. And al-Qadi in one of his two opinions [said]: they are the states which God Most High creates in the body moment by moment. So if He does not create them in it, it becomes non-existent. And al-Nazzam said: it is not permanent, rather He creates it moment by moment, so if He does not create it, it perishes. And most of these sayings are among falsehoods, especially the saying that annihilation is a thing realized externally, and an opposite to permanence, subsisting by itself or in the substance, and that permanence exists not in a locus. And perhaps the aspect of its falsehood is in no need of explanation.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage presents and critiques various theological opinions on the nature of the annihilation (fana') of bodies. It begins by summarizing earlier views on the nature of permanence (baqa'): some say it is an accident subsisting in the body (our companions), some say it is the accidents by which the body is characterized (Imam al-Haramayn), some say it is the states (akwan) (al-Qadi), and al-Nazzam says it is not permanent but created moment by moment. Then it notes that bodies are permanent and susceptible to annihilation, with differences on whether they are eternal or everlasting. The followers of Abu al-Husayn suspended judgment on annihilation, while those who affirmed it differed on its cause. The author then categorizes the opinions into three main views:

1. **First view: Direct annihilation by God.** Al-Qadi and some Mu'tazila hold that God annihilates the world directly without an intermediary. Abu al-Hudhayl says God commands it to perish, and it obeys.

2. **Second view: Annihilation by an opposite (didd).** The majority of Mu'tazila hold that annihilation occurs by the creation of an opposite to the substance, called 'annihilation' itself. Within this, there are four sub-views:
   - Ibn al-Akhshid: annihilation is a non-extended entity localized in a direction; when God creates it, all substances perish.
   - Ibn Shabib: God creates an annihilation in each substance, which then causes non-existence in the next moment.
   - Abu 'Ali and followers: God creates an annihilation for each substance, not in a locus, causing them to perish.
   - Abu Hashim and followers: God creates a single annihilation not in a locus, which annihilates all substances.

3. **Third view: Annihilation by removal of a condition of existence.** Bishr claims the condition is a permanence created by God not in a locus; if it ceases, the substance perishes. The majority of the author's companions and al-Ka'bi hold that permanence subsists in the body and is created moment by moment; if God stops creating it, the substance ceases. Imam al-Haramayn identifies the condition as the accidents necessary for the body; if God does not create them, the body perishes. Al-Qadi in one opinion says it is the states. Al-Nazzam says the body is not permanent but created moment by moment; if God does not create it, it perishes.

After enumerating these opinions, the author dismisses most as falsehoods (abateel), especially the claim that annihilation is a real external entity, an opposite to permanence, subsisting by itself or in the substance, and that permanence exists not in a locus. He says the falsehood is obvious and needs no explanation.

Key Terms
بقاء (baqa')
حالاً فحالاً (halan fa halan)
ضِدّ (didd)
شَرط (shart)
إعدام (i'dam)
مُعْدِم (mu'dim)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which view says that permanence is the states (akwan) created moment by moment?
A) Companions
B) Imam al-Haramayn
C) Al-Qadi
D) Al-Nazzam

Key Takeaway
The debate on annihilation begins with understanding permanence, and three possible mechanisms are introduced.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your very existence at this moment is being created by God anew, how would you live the next moment differently?
?
When you consider that annihilation can occur by the removal of a condition you rely on, what in your life are you treating as a permanent support that only God can sustain?
?
The passage shows scholars deeply pondering the nature of permanence. Have you ever stopped to realize that your own 'permanence' is an illusion? How does that truth shake the way you hold onto worldly things?

Three Main Theories on the Cause of Annihilation (Fana')
Details the three theories of annihilation with sub-views for each.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three main theories on the cause of annihilation (fana') and the various sub-views within each, as debated among theologians.

Core Idea
Theologians proposed three causes for annihilation: direct divine action, creation of an opposite, or cessation of a condition.

In this passage, Sanusi expands on the three categories introduced earlier. For each, he reports the specific positions of various scholars, revealing a rich intra-tradition debate. The first theory holds that God directly annihilates; the second that an opposite called 'annihilation' is created; the third that a condition for existence is removed. Understanding these nuances is crucial for kalam ontology.

Guided Path
1
Read the three main sections
The passage is divided into 'أما الأول' (first), 'وأما الثاني' (second), and 'وأما الثالث' (third). Identify each.
Each section contains multiple sub-views.
2
First theory: Direct removal by God
Al-Qadi says God annihilates without intermediary. Abu al-Hudhayl says God commands 'Perish!'.
Note the contrast: direct vs. command.
3
Second theory: Annihilation by opposite
Majority of Mu'tazila say an opposite called 'fana' is created. Sub-views differ on its locus and number.
Ibn al-Akhshid: localized; Ibn Shabib: in each substance; Abu Ali: each gets one; Abu Hashim: one for all.
4
Third theory: Cessation of a condition
Bishr says condition is a permanence not in a locus; companions say it's a permanence in the body; Imam al-Haramayn says it's the accidents; etc.
Nazzam: body is not permanent but continuously created.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Our companions [hold that] permanence (baqa') is an accident subsisting in the body, which God creates in it moment by moment. And those who affirmed it differed concerning whether annihilation is by the removal of a remover, or by the occurrence of an opposite, or by the removal of a condition. As for the first [view]: al-Qadi and some of the Mu'tazila went that God Most High annihilates the world without intermediary, so it becomes non-existent just as He brought it into existence in that manner, so it became existent. As for the second [view]: the majority of the Mu'tazila went that the annihilation of the substance (jawhar) is by the occurrence of an opposite (didd) to it, namely annihilation. Then they differed: Ibn al-Akhshid went that annihilation, although not extended (mutahayyiz), occurs in a specific direction. And Abu Hashim and his followers said: He creates a single annihilation not in a locus, so by it all the substances become annihilated. As for the third [view]: that the annihilation of the substance is by the cessation of a condition of its existence. Bishr claimed that that condition is a permanence (baqa') which God Most High creates not in a locus, so if it does not exist, the substance becomes non-existent. And the majority of our companions and al-Ka'bi of the Mu'tazila went that it is a permanence subsisting in it, which God Most High creates in it moment by moment. So if God Most High does not create it in it, the substance ceases. And Imam al-Haramayn said that they are the accidents by which the body must be characterized. So if he creates them in it, it perishes. And al-Qadi in one of his two opinions [said]: they are the states which God Most High creates in the body moment by moment. So if He does not create them in it, it becomes non-existent. And al-Nazzam said: it is not permanent, rather He creates it moment by moment, so if He does not create it, it perishes. And most of these sayings are among falsehoods, especially the saying that annihilation is a thing realized externally, and an opposite to permanence, subsisting by itself or in the substance, and that permanence exists not in a locus. And perhaps the aspect of its falsehood is in no need of explanation.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage presents and critiques various theological opinions on the nature of the annihilation (fana') of bodies. It begins by summarizing earlier views on the nature of permanence (baqa'): some say it is an accident subsisting in the body (our companions), some say it is the accidents by which the body is characterized (Imam al-Haramayn), some say it is the states (akwan) (al-Qadi), and al-Nazzam says it is not permanent but created moment by moment. Then it notes that bodies are permanent and susceptible to annihilation, with differences on whether they are eternal or everlasting. The followers of Abu al-Husayn suspended judgment on annihilation, while those who affirmed it differed on its cause. The author then categorizes the opinions into three main views:

1. **First view: Direct annihilation by God.** Al-Qadi and some Mu'tazila hold that God annihilates the world directly without an intermediary. Abu al-Hudhayl says God commands it to perish, and it obeys.

2. **Second view: Annihilation by an opposite (didd).** The majority of Mu'tazila hold that annihilation occurs by the creation of an opposite to the substance, called 'annihilation' itself. Within this, there are four sub-views:
   - Ibn al-Akhshid: annihilation is a non-extended entity localized in a direction; when God creates it, all substances perish.
   - Ibn Shabib: God creates an annihilation in each substance, which then causes non-existence in the next moment.
   - Abu 'Ali and followers: God creates an annihilation for each substance, not in a locus, causing them to perish.
   - Abu Hashim and followers: God creates a single annihilation not in a locus, which annihilates all substances.

3. **Third view: Annihilation by removal of a condition of existence.** Bishr claims the condition is a permanence created by God not in a locus; if it ceases, the substance perishes. The majority of the author's companions and al-Ka'bi hold that permanence subsists in the body and is created moment by moment; if God stops creating it, the substance ceases. Imam al-Haramayn identifies the condition as the accidents necessary for the body; if God does not create them, the body perishes. Al-Qadi in one opinion says it is the states. Al-Nazzam says the body is not permanent but created moment by moment; if God does not create it, it perishes.

After enumerating these opinions, the author dismisses most as falsehoods (abateel), especially the claim that annihilation is a real external entity, an opposite to permanence, subsisting by itself or in the substance, and that permanence exists not in a locus. He says the falsehood is obvious and needs no explanation.

Key Terms
فناء (fana')
جوهر (jawhar)
عَرَض ('arad)
ضِدّ (didd)
إعدام (i'dam)
مُعْدِم (mu'dim)
متحيز (mutahayyiz)
محل (mahall)
حالاً فحالاً (halan fa halan)
شَرط (shart)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what was Abu Hashim's view on annihilation?
A) Annihilation is created in a specific direction.
B) A single annihilation not in a locus annihilates all substances.
C) Annihilation is commanded by God.
D) Annihilation is the removal of a condition.

Key Takeaway
Theologians disagreed on whether annihilation occurs directly, through an opposite, or by removal of a condition, each with detailed variations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
After reading this detailed debate on annihilation, do you feel a greater awe for God's power, or does the complexity trouble you? How does seeing theologians wrestle with these questions affect your own trust in divine wisdom?
?
If the body is sustained moment by moment (as some Ash'aris held), then your very existence is dependent on God's continuous act of preservation. How should this awareness change the way you begin each moment of your day? What specific habit can you adopt to remind yourself of this constant dependence?
?
The theologians were not satisfied with a vague belief in the afterlife; they sought to understand the mechanism of annihilation. Are you willing to invest similar intellectual effort into understanding your faith's doctrines, or do you rely on general slogans? What one theological question will you commit to studying more deeply this week?

Critique of False Opinions on Annihilation
Critiques the majority of opinions on annihilation as falsehoods.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's dismissal of most opinions on annihilation, especially the claim that annihilation is a real entity opposed to permanence.

Core Idea
Sanusi condemns the view that annihilation is a real external thing as an obvious falsehood.

After enumerating the many positions on annihilation, Sanusi delivers a sharp critique. He declares that most of these sayings are falsehoods (abateel), particularly the claim that annihilation is a real entity existing externally, that it is an opposite to permanence, or that permanence exists not in a locus. He says its falsehood requires no explanation. This lesson shows the author's own stance.

Guided Path
1
Read the final sentence
Read the Arabic sentence carefully: 'وأكثر هذه الأقاويل من قبيل الأباطيل...'
Note the strong language.
2
Identify the specifically rejected claims
Sanusi singles out the claim that fana' is a thing realized externally and an opposite to baqa', subsisting by itself or in the substance, and that baqa' exists not in a locus.
These are the metaphysical positions he finds untenable.
3
Reflect on the reason for rejection
Sanusi says 'the aspect of its falsehood is in no need of explanation'. Consider why he thinks it is self-evidently wrong.
It might contradict the basic Kalam understanding that accidents do not subsist by themselves.

أصحابنا بقاء قائم بالجسم يخلق الله فيه حالاً فحالاً. وقال إمام الحرمين الأعراض التي تحت اتصاف الجسم بها. وقال القاضي في أحد قوليه : الأكوان التي يخلقها فيه حالاً فحالاً . وقال النظام : خلقه لأنه ليس بباق، بل يخلق حالاً فحالاً . قد سبقت في مباحث الجسم إشارة إلى أن الأجسام باقية، غير متزايلة على ما يراه النظام، وقابلة للفناء، غير دائمة للبقاء على ما يراه الفلاسفة قولاً بأنها أزلية أبدية . والجاحظ ، وجمع من الكرامية قولاً بأنها أبدية، غير أزلية. وتوقف أصحاب أبي الحسين في صحة الفناء واختلف القائلون بها في أن الفناء بإعدام معدم، أو بحدوث ضد، أو بانتفاء شرط. أما الأول - فذهب القاضي، وبعض المعتزلة إلى أن الله تعالى يعدم العالم بلا واسطة، فيصير معدوماً كما أوجده كذلك ، فصار موجوداً. وذهب أبو الهذيل إلى أنه تعالى يقول له : «افنَ، فيفنى كما قال له : كن فكان . وأما الثاني - فذهب جمهور المعتزلة إلى أن فناء الجوهر بحدوث ضد له الفناء، ثم اختلفوا فذهب ابن الأخشيد إلى أن الفناء، وإن لم يكن متحيزاً، لكنه يكون حاصلاً في جهة معينة . فإذا أحدثه الله تعالى فيها، عدمت الجواهر بأسرها. وذهب ابن شبيب إلى أن الله تعالى يحدث في كل جوهر فناء، ثم ذلك الفناء يقتضي عدم الجوهر في الزمان الثاني . وذهب أبو علي وأتباعه إلى أنه يخلق بعدد كل جوهر فناء لا في محل، فتفنى الجواهر. وقال أبو هاشم وأشياعه يخلق فناء واحد لا في محل، فتفنى به الجواهر بأسرها. وأما الثالث - وهو أن فناء الجوهر بانقطاع شرط وجوده . فزعم بشر أن ذلك الشرط بقاء يخلقه الله تعالى لا في محل، فإذا لم يوجد عدم الجوهر. وذهب الأكثرون من أصحابنا والكعبي من المعتزلة إلى أنه بقاء قائم به، يخلقه الله تعالى حالاً فحالاً. فإذا لم يخلقه الله تعالى فيه، انتفى الجوهر . وقال إمام الحرمين بأنها الأعراض التي يجب اتصاف الجسم بها. فإذا يخلقها الله فيه فني . وقال القاضي في أحد قوليه : هو الأكوان التي يخلقها الله تعالى في الجسم حالاً فحالاً. فمتى لم يخلقها فيه انعدم . وقال النظام إنه ليس بباق، بل يخلق حالاً فحالاً فمتى لم يخلق فني . وأكثر هذه الأقاويل من قبيل الأباطيل ، سيما القول: يكون الفناء أمراً محققاً في الخارج، وضداً للبقاء، قائماً بنفسه، أو بالجوهر، وكون البقاء موجوداً إلا في محل، ولعل وجه البطلان غني عن البيان .
Our companions [hold that] permanence (baqa') is an accident subsisting in the body, which God creates in it moment by moment. And al-Nazzam said: His creation [of it] because it is not permanent, rather He creates it moment by moment. As for the second [view]: the majority of the Mu'tazila went that the annihilation of the substance (jawhar) is by the occurrence of an opposite (didd) to it, namely annihilation. The Nature of Resurrection: Suspension of Judgment
Sanusi presents two views on resurrection and advocates tawaqquf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the debate over whether resurrection is creation after annihilation or gathering of scattered parts, and why the author advocates suspension of judgment.

Core Idea
The true nature of resurrection is rationally inconclusive; one must suspend judgment.

Sanusi introduces the fourth investigation of the sam'iyyat, concerning the nature of the resurrection (al-hashr). Two competing positions are presented: resurrection as a new creation after annihilation, or as a reassembly of scattered parts. Rather than siding with either, Sanusi declares the correct stance to be suspension of judgment (tawaqquf), and then reports—and counters—two proofs for the first view. This lesson unpacks the debate and the reasoning behind tawaqquf.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the concise style of reporting views and proofs.
2
Identify the two positions and the author's verdict
Find where Sanusi states the two views on resurrection and his own position. Note the phrase 'wa-al-haqq al-tawaqquf' (the truth is suspension).
This is the key claim of the passage.
3
Examine the two proofs for the first view
The passage lists two proofs: consensus (ijma') and a Quranic verse. Notice how each is presented and how the first is rebutted.
The second proof is not rebutted explicitly, implying it also falls short.
4
Reflect on why the author suspends judgment
Consider why neither proof is conclusive. The first is denied; the second may have counter-arguments. This leads to tawaqquf.
Tawaqquf is a legitimate theological stance when evidence is balanced.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : المبحث الرابع - واختلفوا في أن الحشر إيجاد بعد الفناء، أو جمع التفرق، والحق التوقف. احتج الأولون بوجوه : الأول - الإجماع قبل ظهور المخالفين ورد بالمنع . الثاني - قوله تعالى : هو الأول والآخر . ولا يتصور إلا بانعدام المخلوقات وليس بعد القيمة ،وفاقاً، فيكون قبلها.
He said: The fourth investigation – And they differed concerning whether the resurrection (al-hashr) is creation after annihilation, or a gathering of what is scattered, and the truth is suspension (al-tawaqquf). The proponents of the first [view] argued with proofs: the first – consensus before the appearance of opponents, and it was rebutted by denial. The second – His statement Most High: 'He is the First and the Last' (57:3). And it cannot be conceived except by the annihilation of created beings, and it is not after the Hereafter, by agreement, so it would be before it.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth investigation (mabhas rabi') concerning the nature of resurrection (al-hashr). Two opposing views are stated: (1) resurrection is creation (by God) after annihilation of the world, and (2) resurrection is a gathering together of what has become scattered (i.e., the physical parts of bodies). The author declares that the correct position is suspension of judgment (tawaqquf). He then reports two proofs given by proponents of the first view (creation after annihilation):

- First proof: consensus (ijma') before the appearance of opponents. This is rejected by countering that such consensus cannot be established (i.e., it is not universally agreed upon).
- Second proof: the Qur'anic verse 'He is the First and the Last' (Surah al-Hadid 57:3). The proponents argue that for God to be the Last, all created beings must first be annihilated, and that this annihilation occurs before the Hereafter (al-qiyama), not after it, so there is creation after that annihilation. The author does not explicitly reject this proof here but implies by his earlier statement that the truth is tawaqquf that the evidence is inconclusive.

Key Terms
الحشر
إيجاد بعد الفناء
جمع التفرق
التوقف
الإجماع
الآخر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One must definitively choose either that resurrection is recreation after annihilation or that it is gathering of parts.
Correction: The author argues that the evidence is inconclusive, so the correct stance is to suspend judgment (tawaqquf).

Checkpoint
What is the author's position on whether resurrection is creation after annihilation or gathering of scattered parts?
A) Creation after annihilation
B) Gathering of scattered parts
C) Suspension of judgment
D) Both are true

Key Takeaway
The resurrection's nature is not rationally decisive; one should suspend judgment between recreation and reassembly.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a disagreement among scholars about a matter of faith, do you tend to side with the majority without thorough investigation? How does Sanusi's example of tawaqquf challenge your willingness to admit ignorance?
?
The author argues that the true nature of resurrection is not rationally conclusive. Does this unsettle you, or does it deepen your reliance on Allah's revelation? Which parts of your belief rest on shaky proofs?
?
Are there theological questions you've been avoiding because they are uncomfortable? What would it mean for you to suspend judgment on something you've always assumed, and live with that uncertainty before Allah?

Consensus as Proof for Resurrection and Its Refutation
Presents the consensus argument and its refutation by denial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the consensus argument for resurrection after annihilation and how it is refuted by simply denying that consensus existed.

Core Idea
Consensus is only valid if it truly exists; denial refutes the claim.

In this lesson, we encounter the first proof presented by proponents of resurrection as creation after annihilation: the claim of early Muslim consensus. The author states this argument and then immediately refutes it by rejecting the premise that there ever was such a consensus. This concise exchange introduces a key method of theological critique—challenging the factual basis of a proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic sentence and its English translation. Note the structure: first the claim (consensus before opponents), then the refutation (denial).
The passage is very concise; every word matters.
2
Understand the consensus argument
Those who believe in resurrection after annihilation argue that early Muslims agreed on this, and no dissenting voice appeared until later. This would make the belief authoritative.
Consensus is a strong proof in Islamic theology.
3
Analyze the refutation
The refutation is simply 'denial'—meaning the claim of consensus is rejected. This could be because later disagreement shows consensus never formed, or because the claim is unverifiable.
Notice that the author does not offer a lengthy argument; the denial itself suffices.
4
Reflect on the method
Ask yourself: Why is denying the existence of consensus a valid refutation? Because if the consensus never existed, the proof collapses.
This shows the importance of verifying the premises of an argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأول - الإجماع قبل ظهور المخالفين ورد بالمنع.
First - consensus before the appearance of opponents, and it was refuted by denial.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This is the first proof presented by those who argue for resurrection as creation after annihilation (al-awwalūn). They claim that there was a consensus (ijmāʿ) among early Muslims that resurrection occurs after annihilation, before any dissenting view appeared. The refutation (jawāb) given here is simply that this consensus is denied (mumtaniʿ) – i.e., the claim of consensus is rejected. The author does not elaborate further, but the point is that the existence of later disagreement shows that consensus never actually held, or that the claim is unsubstantiated.

Key Terms
الإجماع (consensus)
المنع (denial)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That consensus is always a valid proof in theological arguments.
Correction: The consensus argument is only valid if the consensus actually existed. Here, the refutation denies its existence, showing that the mere claim of consensus is not sufficient.

Checkpoint
How is the consensus argument for resurrection after annihilation refuted?
A) By saying the consensus was later abrogated
B) By denying the consensus ever existed
C) By claiming consensus is not a valid source in kalām
D) By saying the consensus only applied to the first generation

Key Takeaway
The consensus argument for resurrection is refuted by denying that the consensus ever existed, showing that no proof can stand on an unsubstantiated premise.
